British Note to Japan Canceling the India-Japan Trade Agreement 24

All British Territories Will Unanimously Boycott Japanese Goods

Japanese Cotton Weaving Industry in a State of Panic, Planning Countermeasures

New Delhi Today, when the Commercial Member of the Viceroy's Executive Council, William, moved a motion in the Legislative Assembly to consider a bill to counter dumping, he declared that the Indian government had taken steps to cancel the 1905 India-Japan Agreement. Today, the Indian government sent an official document to Japan stating that most-favored-nation treatment would be abolished in six months. William declared that the Indian government's step was not out of ill will towards any country, but a completely self-defense plan to alleviate special circumstances, such as currency devaluation, dumping of goods at low prices, etc., all of which would undermine India's industry, etc. (11th National Telegraph)

(London) The Cotton Industry Trade Federation held a meeting in Manchester today regarding the competition between Japan and Lancashire cotton. Mr. Cordon, a Conservative member of Parliament for the Manchester Suburban District, declared that Lancashire is now encountering unprecedented competition. A resolution was passed on the spot requesting the government to impose heavy taxes on foreign goods imported into British colonies, so as to give British commerce a chance to compete. (11th Reuters Telegraph)

New Delhi The Legislative Assembly today passed the Anti-Dumping Bill. The bill authorizes the Indian government to levy import duties on excessively cheap foreign goods that could harm the survival of any industry in India, in order to counter them. The bill was introduced because Indian manufacturers opposed the dumping of Japanese textiles in India. A notice of increased tariffs will be submitted to the Legislative Assembly for approval within two months. The bill will be effective until December 31, 1935. (12th Reuters dispatch)

Japanese Foreign Ministry Received News and Deliberately Showed Calm 25

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs today received official reports that British Foreign Secretary Simon had sent a six-month note yesterday to the Japanese Ambassador to Britain, stating that he intended to cancel the agreement in accordance with Article 4 of the 1904 Japan-India Commercial Treaty. A spokesman for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs elaborated on Britain's move, saying that it was not unexpected, as the British government obviously wanted to open the way for India to pass the Anti-Dumping Law and abolish the most-favored-nation treatment. He also said that Japan would probably try to devise other methods to prevent Japanese commerce with India from being overly shocked, but on the one hand, since it was felt that the existing agreement had to be canceled, it would probably not be easy to negotiate a new agreement. (12th Reuters dispatch)

Osaka Textile Industry Loses Millions of Yuan 26

(Tokyo) According to a telegram from Ambassador Matsudaira in Britain to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, British Foreign Secretary Sir Simon had notified Ambassador Matsudaira that the Japan-India Treaty of Commerce and Navigation of 1904 would expire on October 1st of this year, in order to allow India to break away from the most-favored-nation clause and prevent the dumping of Japanese goods in India. As a result, the Osaka textile industry will suffer losses amounting to millions of yuan. (12th Telegraph dispatch)

Japan Will Appeal to the World Economic Conference 27

(Tokyo) The abrogation of the Japan-India Treaty of Commerce and Navigation has had a great impact on the Japanese cotton industry. Countermeasures are currently being discussed. If the treaty is abrogated, there is a possibility of increased dumping taxes, and after the abrogation notice, after six months, it will be treated as a country without a treaty, and goods from other countries can be taxed at different rates. Therefore, it is difficult to predict the attitude of the Indian government after six months, but at least it will inevitably impose a currency dumping tax. Therefore, textile manufacturers are paying close attention to the tax rate. In addition, the Textile Industry Federation will convene a committee meeting to discuss countermeasures. However, the expansion of the shortening rate after July is inevitable, so before the expiration of the current shortening work period, the current shortening work rate of 27.6% will be further expanded. Some opinions also believe that the issue should be submitted to the World Economic Conference. (12th Telegraph dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs received a telegram this morning from Ambassador Matsudaira in Britain, reporting on India's cancellation of the India-Japan Treaty of Commerce and Navigation, and immediately held a departmental meeting to study countermeasures. It is heard that the following policies have been decided: (1) Trade between Japan and India is gradually becoming closer. At this time, India suddenly cancels the most-favored-nation clause and imposes dumping taxes on Japanese goods. The Japanese government feels very sorry. Not only is it detrimental to the interests of trade between the two countries, but it also deeply hopes that the British government can reconsider the relationship between Japan and Britain. (2) Textile yarn, cotton cloth, and sundries may conflict with the British and Indian industries. It is hoped that the British and Indian governments will still grant most-favored-nation treatment to other commodities that have no impact, such as cement. (3) Sudden changes in tariffs will cause great losses in trade. It is sincerely hoped that the British and Indian governments can adopt a gradual policy. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs telegraphed Ambassador Matsudaira with the above countermeasures, instructing him to earnestly contact the British Foreign Secretary. (12th China United Telegraph)

(Tokyo) The Japanese economic community was very panicked when it received news of India's cancellation of the India-Japan Treaty of Commerce and Navigation, believing that it was the result of the Lancashire cotton yarn industry's strong opposition. After the September 18th Incident, Japanese goods were boycotted in China, and they sought a way out in the South Seas and India, adopting a dumping policy. In India, they competed with British goods. British-produced cotton yarn, cloth, and sundries were defeated. In order to save its domestic industry, the British government cancelled the India-Japan Treaty of Commerce and Navigation to prevent its dumping policy. Current Commentary

Letter on Internal Pacification and External Resistance 36

Our country's national crisis today is becoming increasingly urgent. Externally, the Japanese army is approaching the Great Wall. After the fall of Rehe, eastern Luan is extremely critical. Duolun and Zhangjiakou are also under threat. The Chief of Staff of the Kwantung Army, Koiso Kuniaki, was recently ordered by Mutō to return to Japan. His primary mission is to discuss how to deal with the Middle Eastern Railway issue, and the eagerness to invade Zhangjiakou and Duolun has already become apparent. Internally, the communist bandits are rampant. They have emerged from their old nests and are attempting to expand their area of disturbance. Furthermore, due to the interwoven mountains and rivers of Jiangxi, they can appear and disappear unpredictably. The brave and battle-hardened national army often finds it difficult to cope. Therefore, "internal pacification and external resistance" has now become a particularly important issue. Which should come first should be decided definitively. Now, Chairman Jiang of the Military Affairs Commission has clearly declared the strategy of prioritizing internal pacification before external resistance. If the general officers can muster their courage and follow the exhortations of Chairman Jiang of the Military Affairs Commission, prioritizing the work of "internal pacification" and eliminating the communist bandits in the shortest possible time, establishing general order, and ensuring that the people have food and clothing and can live in peace, then the prospects for resistance against Japan will be greatly improved.

Our country was originally known as an agricultural nation, but the decline of the countryside is worsening year by year. In European and American countries, due to the development of their industries and the expansion of overseas markets, their industries have been able to absorb their surplus population and absorb the floating elements of the countryside, barely maintaining the balance of their society. However, since the outbreak of the world economic crisis, both domestic and foreign markets have felt constricted. The unemployed masses are increasing. Resource-rich countries such as the United States of America are finding it difficult to cope. Skilled nations such as Germany are even resorting to desperate measures. As for Japan, the non-productive nature of military supplies is stimulating the exhausted state of industry in order to absorb surplus production. In this environment, our country's only strategy for absorbing the surplus rural population is to send them abroad to work as coolies in the provinces of Guangdong and Fujian, or to enlist them as soldiers in the interior. The number of reserve workers absorbed by modern cities is ultimately limited. As a result, the national strength is weakening, the national economy is declining, and society is becoming increasingly unstable. At the same time, urban industry and commerce are being fundamentally shaken by the collapse of the rural economy, to the point where they are almost unable to maintain themselves. If this continues, the consequences will be unimaginable. Internal pacification is truly the most urgent issue today.

Therefore, we hope that the authorities will pay attention to the following two points in addition to military action for internal pacification:

First, the stabilization of the people's livelihoods. The majority of our people are on the verge of starvation, from prosperous metropolises to remote villages. Corpses of the starving are seen everywhere, and the unemployed are in droves. Therefore, the first priority of internal pacification must be to open up avenues for the people to survive, so that everyone can use their talents to sustain their lives and contribute their remaining strength to the state and society. It is not easy to make those who have already left agricultural production return to farming (because agriculture is extremely hard work, and even if they return, there may not be land available for cultivation). However, the extra burden on the countryside should be reduced or eliminated, and the exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies should be abolished. This cannot be delayed any longer. As for regulating the rural economy, so that farmers are not subject to high-interest exploitation, and reorganizing existing land, so that land is used to its full potential, then a lopsided society will have a chance to recover, and the prosperity of the cities will have a foundation. The plan for "internal pacification" can then be initially implemented.

Second, the enlightenment of politics. In recent years, active political measures have not been given much attention. Even the minimally required clean government has become the highest ideal. As a result, there are more times of political depression and fewer times of bright hope. The minimum political standards, such as enlightened and clean government, that have already been achieved in European and American democratic countries should be immediately sought to be realized. Our country has a vast territory, and it is truly not easy to achieve immediate results. If county magistrates can be strictly selected and local autonomy can be established, then political clarity can also be expected to be realized.

The above two points, although very brief, are in fact the most urgent tasks for the current "internal pacification." It is necessary to stabilize the people's livelihoods and enlighten politics, and then it will be possible to win the hearts of the people throughout the country and mend the internal and external troubles. This is how it should be in theory.

Japanese Kwantung Army Prepares to Forcibly Seize the Chinese Eastern Railway 37

Secretly Deploying Troops to Various Key Points

Ordering the Puppet Ministry of Communications to Issue a Final Protest

Soviet Russia Continues to Send Goods Trains

Relations Between Japan and Russia Become Increasingly Tense

(Harbin) The Japanese Kwantung Army has decided to forcibly seize the Chinese Eastern Railway. Division Commander Hirose, under the orders of Commander Mutō, secretly deployed the troops of Toyama late at night on the 10th, dispatching them to various key military points. The puppet Railway Protection Army was also ordered to move to various places, seeking opportunities to forcibly remove Soviet railway service personnel and seize the Chinese Eastern Railway, which would then be operated by the South Manchuria Railway Company. (United Chinese News Agency dispatch, 12th)

(Changchun) The Commander of the Kwantung Army today ordered the puppet Ministry of Communications to issue a final protest to the Soviet government, demanding that the Soviet Union return all 83 locomotives, 190 passenger cars, and 3,200 freight cars, totaling 3,473, within one month, or else resort to necessary military action. The South Manchuria Railway Company has newly established a Railway Branch Office in Harbin, with the intention of planning to seize the Chinese Eastern Railway by force. As a result, relations between Japan and Russia are becoming increasingly dangerous. (United Chinese News Agency dispatch, 12th)

(Changchun) According to Japanese newspapers here, the Soviet government in Manchuria once again detained 217 freight cars on the morning of the 10th, guarding against the Japanese side using them to transport military supplies. As a result, the Japanese side is increasingly angered by the Soviet Union. The Deputy Director of the Chinese Eastern Railway visited the puppet Ministry of Communications this morning, requesting that the puppet organization not be used by the Japanese to disrupt international transportation. (United Chinese News Agency dispatch, 12th)

(Harbin) The Japanese organ, the Harbin Times, published an editorial today entitled "Soviet Russia is Naturally Preparing for War," stating that if Soviet Russia were not preparing for war, its bizarre policies would be inexplicable. The locomotives and freight cars seized by Soviet Russia all belong to the Chinese Eastern Railway. More than half of the vehicles owned by the Chinese Eastern Railway have been moved into Russian territory, and the method of removal is tantamount to systematic theft. The Soviet Union's claim that the locomotives were purchased by the Kerensky government and therefore belong to the Soviet government is baseless. If their claim were true, why did the Russian government not move these locomotives into Russian territory years ago? The Soviet Union's explanation proves the Soviet Union's lack of justification and the blatant lies of the Russian authorities. Various contracts clearly prove that the vehicles moved into Russian territory are owned by the Chinese Eastern Railway. The Chinese Eastern Railway is a joint venture between Soviet Russia and "Manchukuo," so any decision related to this railway must be approved by "Manchukuo." Soviet Russia should express its apology for taking without permission, rather than raising the issue of vehicle ownership. The Soviet Union has no choice but to steal vehicles and whitewash its behavior. Speculating on its intentions, can it be said that it is not intentionally preparing for war against Japan, but secretly trying to improve the transport of the absolutely damaged Siberian Railway? "Manchukuo" has repeatedly protested against the removal of vehicles from the Chinese Eastern Railway and suspended traffic, but although Japan and "Manchukuo" are committed to peace with Russia, Soviet Russia has always been preparing for war. Therefore, "Manchukuo's" protests are likely to be ineffective. Japan and "Manchukuo" have no choice but to take the same actions as Soviet Russia. (Reuters dispatch, 12th)

(Harbin) The Soviet representative of the Chinese Eastern Railway, Kessler Ziv, told the representative of Manchukuo (puppet) in Harbin on the afternoon of the 10th that the Manchurian (puppet) side's closure of the railway in Manchuria was illegal, and issued the following protest. The main points of the protest are that the Manchukuo (puppet) officials have closed the junction of the Chabeka and the Middle Eastern Railways, which is an illegal act that hinders international transportation. Please lift the blockade as soon as possible and seek a peaceful resolution. Manchukuo (puppet) issued the following counterattack to this protest, the gist of which is that Manchukuo (puppet) is using its strength to block the connection between the two railways to suppress the illegal actions of the Soviet side and to establish the original mission of the Chinese Eastern Railway's joint operation by Russia and Manchuria, and to promote the Soviet Union's reflection. As for the reason for obstructing this transportation, the responsibility lies with the Soviet Union due to its illegal actions. Manchuria (puppet) is by no means a troublemaker. If the Soviet Union realizes its mistakes and returns the detained vehicles, showing the reality of its reflection, then a peaceful resolution can be established. (Special dispatch, 12th)

(Harbin) Although the officials of Manchukuo (puppet) are doing their best to prevent the Soviet side from carrying freight cars away from the two lines in the Middle East, the Soviet Union took advantage of the lack of border blockade and sent away 70 freight cars on the 8th and 9th, so Manchukuo buried sleepers on the railroad at the junction on the 10th, and resolutely carried out a serious blockade. (Telecommunications dispatch, 11th)

(Tokyo) The representative of the Chinese Eastern Railway (puppet) of Manchukuo, Li Shaogeng, today sent a final notice with a deadline to the representative of the Soviet Union, Kuznesov, as follows: I hope that 83 locomotives, 19 passenger cars, and 3,200 freight cars belonging to the Chinese Eastern Railway that were transported to Soviet Russia will be returned within one month. (Telecommunications dispatch, 12th)

Li Yuanhong's Coffin Arrives in Hongshan 38

Enshrined at Baotong Temple for Scheduled State Funeral

(Hankou) At 8:30 AM on the 12th, the coffins of the late President Li and Madame Wu arrived at Dazhimen from Liujiamiao. Tens of thousands of people from all walks of life came to greet them. At 9:00 AM, the hearse followed the predetermined route, passing through Zhongshan Road and Minquan Road in the French Concession to the wharf. Tens of thousands of mourners, mostly civilians, followed by military and political figures, held funeral streamers. Hundreds of roadside altars were set up along the way. At noon, the coffin was transported across the river by boat, and the navy fired salutes in tribute. When the boat docked at the Dadi Kou in Wuchang, Xia Douyin led all members of the provincial government to greet and pay their respects on the shore. The ceremony was extremely grand. Then, passing through Changjie in front of the provincial government, Xia Douyin again paid his respects alone. When passing Yema Factory, the provincial party headquarters also greeted and paid their respects. At 3:00 PM, it was transported to Hongshan and arrived at 4:00 PM. It was enshrined in Baotong Temple, awaiting the scheduled state funeral and public memorial service. The weather was clear that day, and the streets and lanes were crowded with onlookers, but the order was orderly. The mourners traveled twenty miles back and forth from Hankou to Hongshan without showing any fatigue, which is a testament to the depth of his cherished memory. In particular, a group of wounded soldiers who started the uprising, with broken hands and feet and blind eyes, was the most touching and moving. (Special dispatch, 12th)

(Hankou) When Li's coffin arrived in Hankou on the 12th, the British, Japanese, and German consuls-general and representatives of the French and American consuls were at the station to greet them. When passing through the French Concession, the police all raised their guns in salute. He Chengjun also sent Yang Kuiyi as a representative to pay respects. (Special dispatch, 12th)

Central Political Council Resolves to Abolish the Beiping Political Affairs Committee 39

The Northeast Transportation Committee is Also Resolved to be Abolished

(Nanjing) The Central Political Council held its 352nd meeting at 8:00 AM on the 12th. The following committee members were present: Wang Zhaoming, Ju Zheng, Sun Ke, Chen Guofu, Ye Chucang, Chen Gongbo, Zhang Ji, and Shi Ying, totaling 30 people. Sun Ke presided over the meeting and resolved the following cases:

(1) Resolution on the Standing Committee's proposal on the existence, abolition, and improvement of the administrative system of the Beiping Political Affairs Committee: The Beiping Political Affairs Committee should be abolished, and the improvement of the administrative system should be submitted to the Executive Yuan for review and handling.

(2) The Legislative Group reported on the review and amendment of the Organic Law of the Legislative Yuan. Resolution: Passed according to the original proposal.

(3) The Finance, Military, and Legislative Groups reported on the review of Hunan Province's proposal to organize national salvation loans and national salvation donations. As a result, it was believed that the distribution of the proceeds of the national salvation loans should first be submitted to the Military Affairs Commission for review to determine whether the use is necessary, and then deliberated after receiving a reply. Resolution: Passed according to the review opinion.

(4) The Education Group reported on the review of the primary school curriculum standards, the junior high school Chinese, history, and geography standards, and the senior high school Chinese and history curriculum standards. Resolution: Passed according to the review opinion.

(5) The Education Group reported on the review of the reorganization of national music. Resolution: Submitted to the Executive Yuan and the Central Research Institute for review.

(6) Resolution: The Northeast Transportation Committee should be abolished immediately by order.

(7) Resolution: The draft Supplementary Regulations for Punishing Military Police should be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review.

(8) The Finance Group proposed a four-point standard to promote the negotiation of the budget for the 22nd year of the Republic. Resolution: Submitted to the heads of the five yuan, the Minister of Finance, and Committee Member Chen Guofu for review.

(9) Resolution: Talented people from the four provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe who have fled to the interior should be properly discussed by the Executive and Examination Yuans to determine how to employ them. (Central News Agency dispatch, 12th)

(Nanjing) Sun Ke, Ma Chaojun, Chuan Bingchang, Chen Gongbo, Fu Rulin, and Shen Shuyu, Director of the Customs Administration, returned to Beijing from Shanghai on the morning of the 11th. Aizawa Delivers Speech in Beiping Believing That the Time for Direct Negotiations is Not Yet Ripe 40

(Beiping) Former Japanese Foreign Minister Aizawa arrived in Beiping yesterday afternoon. Today, he told a Reuters reporter that his visit to China was entirely a private affair with no political relationship and that the sole purpose was to conduct an on-site investigation to understand the state of the general situation. He believes that the time for direct negotiations is not yet ripe. In his opinion, the general public opinion and public sentiment of both countries do not allow for the opportunity for direct negotiations. Later, when the Reuters reporter asked him when he would consider it ripe, he said, "This kind of opportunity will definitely come one day, but I cannot predict it." Aizawa also said that he had met with Chinese people in Shanghai, but he did not want to meet with Chinese leaders because this would make things difficult for them. He also attended a banquet for famous Chinese people in Beiping, but no political affairs were discussed at the dinner. When the issue of the mandated islands was discussed, he resolutely said that Japan would protect them no matter what. The Japanese Embassy will hold a banquet tonight to welcome Aizawa. It is said that the ambassadors of various countries will participate. Aizawa will leave for Dalian tomorrow afternoon to return to his country. (Reuters dispatch, 12th)

The library plans to first repair the missing tripod ears and other parts, arrange them in boxes and on tables according to their original positions, and send them for preservation. In addition, many stone chamber tombs from the Han Dynasty have been discovered in Teng County, and there are more than a thousand Han paintings on stones in the Cao Wang tomb. Washington Economic Talks Promote International Cooperation 50

Abandoning the Diplomatic Isolation Policy Adopted for the Past Eight Years

The Meeting Will Only Freely Exchange Views and Make No Agreements

The U.S. Is Prepared to First Remove Tariff Barriers to Advocate for All Countries

The Japanese Government Decides to Appoint Viscount Ishii as Representative

(London) News received tonight: President Roosevelt invited the British Prime Minister to Washington, D.C. with the following words: "Please come and stay with me for a week. I believe that in this week, we can do more for God than we have done before." It is now known that the upcoming talks will be a free exchange of opinions, and the scope of the talks will be extremely broad, including the entire war debt issue, the date of the World Economic Conference, tariff policy issues, international exchange rates, world trade, methods of cooperation in the League of Nations disarmament conference, and the general situation in Europe, all of which will be discussed. The purpose of this meeting is only to exchange opinions and not to make any agreements. The result of this talk will be to promote closer cooperation between the United Kingdom and the United States. It is now believed that British Prime Minister MacDonald will not allow British war debts to become an international issue of even greater scope. What is being discussed now is only a general discussion of the war debt issue. (Reuters, 11th)

(New York) General opinion is that the upcoming international talks in Washington, D.C. will be sufficient to promote the United States to abandon its isolationist policy adopted for the past eight years. According to Secretary of State Hull, the purpose of the Washington talks is only to prepare for the World Economic Conference. President Roosevelt will request full authority from Congress to negotiate treaties with various countries. Hull and British Ambassador Lindsay both believe that stabilizing currency prices, using more silver coins, and limiting silver production are all urgent tasks. (Havas, 11th)

Japan Seeks to Ease Anti-American Sentiment: Ishii Chosen as Representative 51

(Tokyo) Japanese Foreign Minister Kōsai Uchida entered the Imperial Palace at 10:00 AM this morning to meet with the Emperor and report on the circumstances of participating in the World Economic Conference. He left the Imperial Palace at 11:00 AM and immediately telegraphed Ambassador Debuchi to reply to the U.S. State Department. After consultation between Uchida and Saitō, the Japanese representative was decided to be Kikujirō Ishii, emphasizing the easing of Japanese-American sentiment, with the goal of having the United States recognize Japan's Far Eastern policy. Therefore, a veteran of the diplomatic community was appointed to this position, and economic and financial experts were appointed as his advisors. Masatake Yamaguchi, Secretary-General of the Seiyūkai, commented: "Ishii is undoubtedly an elder statesman of the diplomatic community, but the purpose of this meeting is financial and economic. It is unknown how much specialized knowledge Ishii actually has. To achieve the desired goals of this conference, the position of advisor is very important." Minseitō Secretary-General Matsuda commented that Takahashi, Yamamoto, Wakatsuki, and Shidehara can no longer participate, and there is no one more suitable than Ishii. Although this meeting emphasizes economics, from Japan's standpoint, it should focus on U.S.-Japan diplomatic relations, taking the opportunity to develop friendly relations between the two countries, break through the deadlock in the Pacific issue, and make the recognition of Japan's status in the Far East by the United States the most important task. (China United Press, 12th)

(Tokyo) Ishii will represent the Japanese government at the talks on international issues in Washington, D.C. After the Washington discussions are completed, Ishii will go to London to participate in the World Economic Conference. Japanese Ambassador to the United Kingdom Matsudaira is expected to be the overall Japanese representative at the conference. Since Ishii is a politician rather than an economic expert, his appointment as Japanese representative proves that Japan's concern for the Washington talks is more political than economic. Ishii has served as Japanese Foreign Minister, Ambassador to the United States, Ambassador to France, and Chief Representative to the League of Nations, and is now sixty-seven years old. (Reuters, 12th)

U.S. Bans Publication of Diplomatic Secrets, Aiming to Maintain U.S.-Japan Friendship 52

(Washington) Today, members of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee announced that the State Department's request for legislation to prevent the publication of secret diplomatic documents and to protect the U.S. diplomatic secret codes is solely intended to prevent Yatterley from publishing his newly compiled book on Japanese diplomatic secrets, so as not to hinder U.S.-Japan friendship. This case has now been re-drafted by the Senate Foreign Relations Committee and submitted to the Senate plenary session today, with only those who leak secret codes among federal employees being subject to criminal penalties. (National Telegraph, 11th)

Lowering Tariffs Is an Urgent Task 53

(Washington) U.S. Secretary of State Hull stated today that President Roosevelt will begin negotiating to lower tariffs worldwide before convening an economic conference in London, and will ask Congress to first lower U.S. tariffs before that day to show good faith. Legislation is currently being drafted to be submitted to Congress, and in addition to generally reducing tariffs, the President also plans to seek smoother international trade through reciprocal agreements. In addition, Hull freely expressed his personal opinions on the tariff issue, saying that the current thirteen million unemployed men and women are sufficient proof that unprecedented high tariffs cannot protect U.S. industry. The Republican argument that striving to lower tariffs will flood the U.S. market with foreign goods has become an outdated concept. It must be understood that the basis of international trade lies entirely in mutually beneficial exchange of goods, but high tariffs everywhere make this kind of exchange impossible. Therefore, for its own sake, the United States should immediately lower tariffs, and it is expected that today's Democratic Congress will undoubtedly reduce them quickly. (National Telegraph, 11th)

War Debts and Trade Will Be Considered Together 54

(Washington) Regarding the war debt issue, the State Department today stated that it could not apply a universal approach and made no other comments. However, according to those close to the government, the plan that the United States will propose to the major countries is so broad in nature that the President will ask Congress to authorize all substantive contributions to war debts. It is expected that when the President requests authorization to conclude reciprocal tariff agreements, he will also request the power to reorganize or modify the war debt repayment procedures. Moreover, a certain economic expert who often contributes opinions to the government now believes that war debts and trade will be considered simultaneously in the Washington talks. Several members of Congress also believe that if the President can advocate for a reasonable international purchase of silver to stabilize silver prices, then a majority in Congress will be happy to agree to authorize the President to adjust war debts. It was also heard today that several Democratic leaders in the Senate are planning to first pass a resolution through Congress to advise the President to take certain steps regarding war debts, so as to avoid the President having to request special privileges. (National News Agency, 11th)

Top-Level Guest Treatment for Herriot 55

(Washington) Former French Prime Minister Herriot came to the United States as a "free observer" to hold economic talks. The White House will treat him as a top-level guest, just like British Prime Minister MacDonald. Herriot is scheduled to depart from France on the 17th, and his trip has actually been advanced. He will stay at the White House at the same time as MacDonald, but President Roosevelt will meet with them separately. (Havas, 12th)

Small Countries Deeply Disappointed at Being Excluded 57

(Washington) Today, several parties pointed out that the U.S. State Department has made a mistake in the way it invited other countries to discuss economic war debt issues. According to reliable sources, the Little Entente and Poland felt slighted because the United States did not invite them to send special representatives. The feelings of Poland and Czechoslovakia were particularly deep. Today, their ambassadors to the United States went to the State Department to inquire when they could negotiate, but the State Department replied that the United States would be happy to discuss trade and currency issues through normal diplomatic channels, but would not invite special envoys to be sent. This reply quickly spread to other embassies, and Belgium, Romania, and Yugoslavia were all deeply disappointed. However, it is expected that after hearing the replies received by the Polish and Czech ambassadors, they may not go to the State Department to inquire again. Although this discussion mainly focuses on economic issues, it is said that war debts will also be discussed separately with representatives from various countries. The smaller countries of Europe are deeply concerned that after the United States has agreed on a war debt solution with the United Kingdom, France, and Italy, it will attempt to apply the same approach to smaller debtor countries, so they all want to be invited to talk in order to avoid this move. (National Telegraph, 11th)

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull issued a statement regarding the future economic talks, saying that the U.S. government invited a small number of countries, treating them equally, according to a precise plan. We want to consult with the representatives of the invited countries separately, and the representatives of the uninvited countries in Washington will also be treated with the same sincere attitude. Previously, foreign representatives here believed that the upcoming preliminary talks were extremely important internationally, and they were quite surprised that their countries had not been invited. It was said that for the World Economic Conference to succeed, several countries should have the opportunity to speak during the preliminary talks. For example, it would be beneficial to consult Czechoslovakia on tariff issues and Romania on wheat and kerosene issues. Therefore, the State Department announced the above declaration to comfort the Little Entente and other uninvited countries, fearing that the number of representatives would be too large and the talks would turn into a conference, making President Roosevelt's proposal difficult to succeed, so only a small number of countries were invited. (Havas, 12th)

After Several Twists and Turns, the Four-Power Talks Are Gradually Settled 83

The Principle of the British, Italian, French, and German Peace Pact Is Established

Efforts Are Being Made to Make Its Provisions Meet French Reservations

Mussolini Expresses Optimism About the Future

National News Agency, Rome, 11th The reliable sources here announced today that the Four-Power Peace Pact proposed by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini has been accepted in principle by the United Kingdom, France, and Germany. Efforts are now being made to make its wording compliant with French reservations. It is reported that Mussolini does not insist on the wording of the pact, as long as the spirit of maintaining peace is preserved. France has raised some reservations, especially regarding Poland and the Little Entente, and insists that it cannot force small countries to comply with the text. After repeated talks between Mussolini and the representatives of the three countries, an understanding has been reached on several key points of the pact, such as Germany's restoration of armaments and revision of the treaty. As for all the detailed provisions, they will be gradually drafted, but Mussolini is confident that full and satisfactory agreement can ultimately be obtained.

Italian-German-Austrian Rome Conference: Mussolini Receives Austrian Chancellor 84

National News Agency, Rome, 11th The Italian capital has now become a focus of global attention. The Moscow "Blue Room" English Engineer Case Opens 85

Accusation Read in Court in Russian

Accused of Counter-Revolutionary Sabotage

Reuter, Moscow, 12th -- The trial of six engineers from the Vickers Company opened this afternoon. The courtroom was very crowded with spectators. Before the clock struck twelve, five English defendants were brought into court, placed in the dock, guarded by two Red Army soldiers. Soon after, the sixth Englishman, MacDonald, also joined them, his beard long and his eyes sunken. The Russian defendants, except for one who was ill, also entered the dock one after another. A platform was placed in the courtroom, covered with red cloth, guarded by more than ten soldiers. Seated on the platform were officials, lawyers, and journalists. The judge entered the courtroom in plain clothes, and everyone stood up. The presiding judge then opened the court and asked the defendants about their age, occupation, and nationality. MacDonald's answers were very faint and almost inaudible. The court clerk, carrying a large number of case files, read the indictment into the microphone. The defendants were allowed to sit down while it was being read. At the same time, troops patrolled the streets outside the courthouse to prevent public gatherings. The reading of the Soviet Russian indictment took a long time. It began by mentioning the counter-revolutionary activities of saboteurs in the electrical plants, accusing the saboteurs of (1) destroying the electrical plants in order to ruin Soviet industry and weaken the Soviet state, (2) collecting and using secret important military and civilian information to hinder the Soviet Union, and (3) bribing employees of the electrical plants to carry out their counter-revolutionary sabotage activities. A special Soviet expert committee reported that the failures of the electrical plants were due either to criminal negligence or to deliberate sabotage, one or the other. The indictment made the following accusations against the six English defendants: (1) Vickers Company engineer Gregory belonged to a counter-revolutionary sabotage party, engaged in economic, military, and civilian espionage, and passed the information he obtained to Thornton. (2) Krushni belonged to a sabotage party and, in his capacity as an installation engineer, engaged in systematic economic and military espionage. At the Yakou Electrical Plant, he arranged for sabotage activities, deliberately misinstalling electrical machinery, causing the plant to fail, and systematically bribing Russian engineers and workers to commit espionage and sabotage. (3) MacDonald, in his capacity as an installation engineer, participated in sabotage activities at the Slatoust and Zugres electrical plants, followed Thornton's instructions, collected much secret military information, investigated the production of armaments and ammunition, and instructed Russian engineers to commit sabotage, resulting in repeated damage to the electrical plants. The amount of his bribes totaled 10,000 rubles. (4) Vickers Company's Russian manager, Monkhouse, belonged to a counter-revolutionary party with the following counter-revolutionary aims: (a) collecting secret military and civilian information, (b) participating in sabotage activities, (c) bribing two Russian engineers to reward them for their espionage and sabotage activities, and (d) bribing Russian engineers to conceal defects in the installed machinery. (5) Vickers engineer Nordwall belonged to a counter-revolutionary party, instructed workers to sabotage the electrical plant during the installation of machinery at Ivgres, and bribed workers 5,000 rubles to conceal defects in the Vickers Company's installation. (6) Thornton, Monkhouse's chief assistant, also belonged to a counter-revolutionary party, engaged in espionage on technical, military, and civilian matters, and ordered his subordinates MacDonald and Krushni, as well as many Russian engineers and workers, to carry out sabotage activities at several electrical plants. He also bribed engineers and workers to commit espionage, sabotage, and conceal defects in the installed machinery. The events described by the prosecutor began in 1927 and ended in 1932. Twelve Russian employees of the Vickers Company, including the female secretary Kadusov, were also among those accused. The evidence included confessions obtained by the political police from Russian employees under duress. The indictment also stated that MacDonald had confessed to his crimes, but the other Englishmen completely denied the charges, admitting only to minor gifts to Russian engineers and workers, occasional defects in machinery that had been repaired, and collecting information beneficial to the Vickers Company. After the indictment was read, MacDonald and the twelve Russian defendants pleaded guilty, but the other five Englishmen pleaded not guilty.

MacDonald Confesses, Startling the Entire Courtroom 86

National, Moscow, 12th -- When the trial of six British Vickers Company engineers accused of espionage, sabotage, and bribery opened this afternoon in the Moscow Trade Union Hall, the defendant MacDonald confessed to the crime of sabotage. This action was completely unexpected, and when announced, the entire courtroom was shocked and order was disrupted. In addition, eleven Russian accomplices, including one woman, also confessed to their crimes. However, the remaining British engineers, Monkhouse, Thornton, Krushni, Nordwall, and Gregory, all pleaded not guilty. Today, Soviet officials, diplomats, and journalists were present to observe the trial, so when it opened at 12:05, the audience was already full. First, the prosecutor read the indictment, which was eighty pages long and detailed MacDonald's confession during the Russian officials' investigation of the case regarding the sabotage of power plants. It was stated that MacDonald confessed that his goal was to hinder the manufacture of Soviet military materials, and his plan was to destroy power plants in wartime. He had told Russian engineers, such as Gusev, about this conspiracy. As for the Russian woman, Kutuzova, who worked as a secretary for Vickers Company, she was accused of giving bribes to another Russian man, Ulenik, who was also a Russian employee of Vickers Company, and was accused of accepting bribes and sabotage. At 3:30, after the indictment was read, the court adjourned and reconvened at 6:00 PM. The British Chargé d'Affaires, Sterling, and other members of the British Embassy were also present to observe the trial.

British House of Lords Passes Goods Restriction Bill 87

Reuter, London, 11th -- As the trial of six British engineers in Moscow was about to begin, the British House of Lords unanimously passed the third reading of the bill prohibiting the import of Russian goods. Secretary of War Hailsham stated that the Vickers Electrical Company had a commercial relationship with the Soviet Union for many years, and the company currently had uncompleted contracts worth 1.5 million pounds, so it was in the company's interest to be friendly with the Russian government. He also stated that the British Ambassador to Russia had visited the detainees and was surprised that the British engineers were so frightened after being imprisoned for three days that they dared not speak. If three days could have such an effect on Englishmen or Scotsmen, then one could imagine the influence of Russian prisons. The British government sincerely hoped that it would not be necessary to exercise the power of this bill, but the government was determined to do everything possible to secure justice for the British citizens in Moscow. Former Colonial Secretary Passfield criticized the bill but welcomed the government's statement that it would not use the power of the bill except to protect the six engineers.

Russian Newspaper Cites British-German Incident 88

TASS, Moscow, 12th -- The Soviet government newspaper "Izvestia" today, in an editorial, compared the British government's different attitudes towards the detention of British nationals in Germany and the Soviet Union. The British government's attitude towards the German authorities' detention of British national Fraser can be seen in Simon's reply to a question in the House of Commons on April 10. At that time, Simon only said that Fraser was accused of preparing to commit a major espionage crime and that diplomatic channels would be used to inquire about the details of the charges. The newspaper said that when the Soviet authorities detained several British citizens, the charges against them had already been published in the newspapers. When a British national was detained by the German fascists, he was only accused of the vague charge of preparing to commit a major espionage crime. What was the British Foreign Office's response to these two cases? The Soviet accusations were dismissed as baseless before they were even published, while the German fascists seemed to be trusted. The Soviet detention of British nationals provoked immediate protests and threats, but the British Foreign Secretary considered protesting the German detention of British nationals to be meddling. What can be seen here is that the British Foreign Office is applying two different means and strategies to the Soviet Union and fascist Germany. Of course, we do not want to urge Britain to take any kind of measures against Germany. What we are concerned with is that the anti-Soviet movement related to the case of the Vickers Company employees being accused and the means that the British government wants to take in this case are clearly inconsistent with the interests of the British defendants in this case. The British government is only obeying the wishes of the anti-Soviets and wants to use this case to destroy British-Soviet commercial relations and embark on a path of open anti-Soviet policy.

King of the World's Trees 92

Trunk Diameter Exceeds Eleven Yards

(Reuter, Belgrade Correspondence) In the Bosnian mountains of Yugoslavia, in the village of Rankovic, there is an oak tree that is probably the king of the world's trees. Its trunk is more than eleven yards in diameter and hollow, like a giant room that can hold seventy or eighty people. In strong winds and rain, shepherds often drive their flocks into it for shelter.

Sketches of a Journey North (1) By Our Special Correspondent, Guo An 93

"Going to the front line to report the news!"

I boarded the train with such impassioned emotions, bid farewell to my beloved Shanghai. A long snake-like train rushed forward through the dawn wind and morning mist. My wife, watching me leave her, gradually receding into the distance, her eyes immediately turned red. I knew that she was feeling bitter inside, but you should not be sad at my departure to the front line, you woman are truly weak.

Iron wheels raced across the green fields, passing through those beautiful little villages. My head was pressed tightly against the train window, gazing at the countryside on all sides, while in my heart, I was echoing the emotions of last year's January 28th Incident. But what have those iron-willed national warriors of ours, and those nameless heroes who died for the defense war, left behind here? The blood-stained trenches and the beehives under the enemy's bombs have already faded into a misty blur. In the embrace of this maiden-like spring, aren't the pink peach blossoms still smiling in the spring breeze? The train passed Huangdu and quickly arrived at Qingyang Port. The bridge at Qingyang Port gave me a very brief but painful memory. The train slowly crawled across the iron bridge, and I saw Kunshan and the upright tower body. The wheel of time has already destroyed the shadows of sorrow, misery, and grief. The pagodas of Suzhou and the pagodas of Wuxi are both "standing at attention" unharmed in the spring breeze. Isn't this how the beauty of Jiangnan is expressed? The Jinshan Temple in Zhenjiang overlooks the sails in the river. On the moist yellow soil cliff, those coolies' huts still occupy the land. I saw this reality of heaven and hell, and I could only sit down in silence and light a cigarette, using the wisps of smoke to blur my own sentimentality.

When I saw the majestic and solemn Nanjing city walls through the train window, suddenly the gentle sky scattered a light-footed breeze, treading on the green fields, slowly playing the tune of "Spring Will Not Last Long." On the ridge, new graves covered with yellow earth, crouched the "magpie" with its black and white flowers intermingled. It lived naturally on the earth, but as I looked at this tender green after Qingming, and looked north towards the beacon fires of my homeland, the fathers and elders under the iron hooves, then I only felt a sourness in my nose.

The connecting train continued to Nanjing riverside at five o'clock in the afternoon. Many passengers crossing the river crowded onto the ferry. Looking south at Lion Mountain, looking east at the rolling waves of the river, this is the territory of the great Republic of China, but the foreign warships parked in the heart of the river proudly raised the flags of imperialism. Our toy-like small gunboats, so small, lay down in front of those huge foreign warships, but the flag of the Blue Sky, White Sun, and Red Earth was also fluttering on the bow.

The scene at Pukou felt almost the same as the scene at dusk. In the ticket office, many gray soldiers were still sleeping. On the cold and deserted platform, a blue steel train ready to go straight to Beiping was parked. Military police and police officers, plus a few scattered dozens of passengers, decorated the large Pukou Railway Station.

There were twenty or so people in the Red Swastika Society's ambulance team, also heading north on this train. They were working hard to fulfill their national obligations, so they did not linger on the spring colors of Jiangnan, and were willing to step on the road of resisting Japan. Furthermore, they were willing to drop their stretchers and take up guns. Then, can China be guaranteed not to perish? I was too hasty and did not ask in detail where they came from, and who initiated and organized them, but I dare to say one thing, they are Chinese. They have clearly recognized the gravity of the fact that national demise is imminent. They are organized by their passion and conscience. In my heart, I express my respect to them.

Xuzhou was still surrounded by sand and soil. Because it was early in the morning, the scene at the station, apart from some hawkers wearing blue cloth cotton jackets, was gray soldiers. A very sharp morning wind was blowing at the station. The green in the fields was similar to that in Jiangnan, but the intoxicating spring breeze could not be found here. Soon the train leaped again towards the vast plains of the north.

The sunlight shone very softly on the earth. The fields on the plains were neatly arranged with green velvet-like wheat fields. The mountains in the distance showed their tall and majestic appearance, flying in the hazy clouds. The gentle outline of the mountains of Jiangnan could not be seen here. The neat villages, and the faces of those Shandong farmers full of antique flavor, as well as the little-footed women, wearing blue cloth clothes and pink ribbons wrapped around their feet. In these expressions, the Shandong people are the great ones under the wheel of time.

I looked out the train window, as if I was very concerned about these Shandong folks. I witnessed the present situation of being well-fed and warmly clothed, and swept away all the impressions of Shandong's crying hunger and displacement in my mind from five or six years ago. Especially when the train arrived at Zhangxia Station, the beautiful mountain bay to the west, with thousands and hundreds of houses, snow-white pear blossoms, and tender willows blown open by the spring breeze, I really missed this beautiful Zhangxia Bay. Moreover, the Shandong tea room said to me, "Sir, this place is really beautiful. Peaches and pears are produced especially abundantly every year. The railway bureau really needs to take out money to build it a little. Then, rich people can also come to play." He said this, and I only nodded, admitting that he was right. 民房 near Sanyingtun destroyed by enemy aircraft (Central News Agency photo)

The city walls of Yanzhou were becoming more incomplete day by day. Our train entered the station at twelve o'clock. Needless to say, the oily smoked chicken was being shouted by the Shandong folks. There were many soldiers on the station platform, all taking off their upper military clothes, white sweat vests, very neatly all the same white, filling the road there. Red and black faces dripping with sweat. I took a picture against the wooden fence of this powerful expression, turned around and said to the policeman at the station, "Whose team is this, so neatly organized?" "This is Lao Han's team," he replied in a tone of certainty. It seemed like he looked closely again. The armed soldiers at the station seemed to have very neat clothes, and the guns were also good, mostly "Czech style." The appearance of each soldier was somewhat attractive. "Well, this kind of army is indeed not bad, no wonder Song Zheyuan's big knife team made a splash at Xifengkou." I thought so in my heart when the train started.

Chen Jintai, a wounded soldier of the 29th Army, once killed dozens of enemies with a big knife (Central News Agency photo)

The train arrived in Jinan at 6:20 PM. The weather immediately cooled down, with gusts of cold wind blowing. Indeed, people who are used to living in Jiangnan, coming out of the warm embrace, suddenly encountering this cold force, really feel a little trembling. I patrolled the station and felt that this Jinan station, which is quite well-built, can be counted as one of the best in North China. The best impression was that there was not a single idle soldier wandering around the station. Except for a dozen or so soldiers on duty, I simply looked around for a long time and couldn't find one. The platform was also cleaned, and everything was very orderly. When the train started, I was again pondering this relatively good impression.

A friend in a suit, who boarded from Jinan, was sitting across from me. He was an employee of a Jinan automobile company. So, during the chat, Lao Han of Shandong became good material for our temporary conversation. "How is Han X in Shandong?" "He can be considered a good person," he answered like that after contemplating for a long time. "I heard that many cases, he has to intervene himself, almost none of them go through the court." "There is no way, the common people only want to sue him when they file a lawsuit, he set up a room for the common people to sue, and the common people are allowed to sue and he would give an audience immediately, and quickly resolve the matter, so in this way, greedy officials and bullies dare not be rampant, especially for those who smoke white powder and eat opium, he has really shot a lot of them." "He is really a good official who doesn't want money." "But he himself doesn't want money, I'm afraid his subordinates will take advantage of his nodding off to take money privately, but he is too fierce, so this kind of problem is not seen."

Japanese Warships Concentrated in Hankou 94

Twelve Warships Arriving Continuously

Japanese Concession Checks Chinese Entering and Exiting

Hankou Correspondence, since the fall of Rehe, the Japanese are trying to disturb our hinterland and disrupt the rear. The Yangtze River area has become their point of attention. It was rumored last month that Japan decided to concentrate its navy in Shanghai, Nanjing, and Hankou to give our side the greatest threat. Judging from the current situation, it is not without reason. It has been found that no more than two Japanese warships were normally stationed in Hankou. After the Mukden Incident occurred, four or five ships were stationed. Recently, only four warships, the Ataka, Futami, Tsushima, and Kotaka, were in Hankou. In terms of protecting Japanese residents, it was more than sufficient. Unexpectedly, on the 7th, 8th, and 9th, three ships, the Sumida, Atami, and Katata, opened to Hankou. At 4:00 PM on the 10th, five more ships arrived, the Uji, Momo, Yanagi, Kashi, and Hinoki, totaling twelve warships. The ships were connected stem to stern, and the situation was gradually becoming serious. The Japanese Naval Commander stationed in Hankou is still Sakano, who is responsible for the highest command. It is said that the Japanese ships were summoned by Sakano. There is also Lieutenant Commander Muto, who is in charge of liaison between Shanghai and Hankou, who went to Shanghai last month and is now in Hankou. The number of troops stationed on each ship varies, and they often land to practice warfare. Our authorities believe that Wuhan is calm, and the arrival of a large number of Japanese warships may cause panic, so they made a special appointment to ask the Japanese consul about the situation. How he replied is not yet known. Recently, a radio station was set up in the Japanese Concession to communicate directly with Tokyo and the three northeastern provinces. They are paying extraordinary attention to Chinese people entering and exiting. Not long ago, they conducted inspections or made illegal arrests. Although the inspection has now stopped, the reconnaissance is even stricter. In addition, they are paying more attention to stockpiling food and selling goods, all of which are bought by Chinese collaborators. However, many Wuhan merchants are quite aware and few are fooled, and the sluggish sales of goods are even more of a major blow to them. The Japanese Chamber of Commerce has held meetings to ask the authorities to find ways to provide relief. Commander Sakano and the Japanese consul have also held secret meetings twice to decide on measures. (April 11)

Cai Tingkai's Pre-Departure Arrangements 95

Xu Jing Tang Presides Over the Pacification Headquarters

Mao Weisou Presides Over the 19th Army

Deng Shizeng Goes to the Front Lines to Suppress Bandits

Each Regiment Commander Secures the Rear's Security

Fuzhou Communication: Cai Tingkai, due to the tense military situation of bandit suppression on the Fujian border, and his need to go to Guangdong to negotiate aid for Jehol, specially invited Xu Jing Tang, former commander of the 5th Army of the National Revolutionary Army, to Fujian to serve as the chief advisor of the Pacification Headquarters, presiding over the internal affairs of the headquarters, so that Chief of Staff Deng Shizeng could go to the front lines to command the military. Cai himself could also go to Guangdong on a chosen day. Xu, upon receiving Cai's telegram invitation in Hong Kong, took a ship from Hong Kong to Xiamen on the 31st of last month. On the 1st of this month, he went from Xiamen to Zhangzhou to discuss everything with Cai. On the 2nd, he returned to the province via Xiamen from Zhangzhou, arriving on the 4th and immediately staying at the Pacification Headquarters. On the 5th, he visited Gushan with Jiang Guangnai and discussed military and political issues of the province. On the 6th, the Pacification Headquarters officially sent a letter to hire Xu as the chief advisor. Deng Shizeng took a plane to Zhangzhou at 1 PM in the afternoon to meet Cai, to negotiate the key points of bandit suppression, and then went to the front lines to supervise the army. As for Cai, he took a plane from Zhangzhou to Quanzhou on the 3rd to meet with Division Commander Mao Weisou, reportedly planning to appoint Mao as the deputy commander of the 19th Army, so that he would act as the army commander after Cai's departure. On the 4th, he returned to Zhangzhou by plane from Quanzhou and instructed Division Commanders Shen Guanghan and Qu Shounian to be responsible for the military affairs in western Fujian, and Division Commanders Liu Heding and Lu Zhenbang to be responsible for the military affairs in northern Fujian. Also, to consolidate the security of the rear, he specially appointed Li Jinbo, commander of the 1st Special Regiment of the 19th Army, as the commander of bandit suppression in Longxi and Nanjing counties; Chen Renzhi, commander of the 1st Regiment of the Supplementary Brigade, as the commander of bandit suppression in Zhanghai, Chengping, Zhao'an, and Xiao'an counties; Sun Lanquan, commander of the 2nd Regiment of the Supplementary Brigade, as the commander of bandit suppression in Changtai and Hua'an counties; and Deng Xingcha, commander of the 3rd Regiment of the Supplementary Brigade, as the commander of bandit suppression in Tongan and Anxi counties, ordering them to clear up the scattered bandits within their defense areas within a limited time. As for Cai himself, he plans to go to Guangdong with Chief of Staff Huang Qiang and others of the headquarters within the next two or three days, to lead the strong soldiers of the Southwest and go north to fight the enemy. (April 7th)

Former President Li's Coffin Arrives in Hankou from Tianjin 97

All Circles of Wuhan Go to the Station to Greet It

Temporarily Placed in Hongshan Before a National Funeral Is Scheduled

Hankou Communication: The former President of the Republic, Li Songqing of Huangpi, passed away in Tianjin the year before last. The National Government, in remembrance of the founding meritorious official, decided to hold a national funeral. On the 8th of this month, the coffins of Li and his wife, Mrs. Wu, were transported from Hannan. Li's widow, Mrs. Li, Li's eldest son, Shaoji, second son, Shaotang, daughter, Shaofen, and grandchildren accompanied the coffin southward. A platoon of soldiers dispatched by Yu Xuezhong guarded the group. There were a total of five cars, allocated by the Ministry of Communications, one carrying the coffin, one carrying the family members, and the rest carrying the staff of the National Funeral Preparatory Office and guards. At 9:00 AM on the 11th, they arrived at Liujiamiao Station. Because the Welcoming Coffin Office requested a temporary stop for one day, the train stopped immediately and was scheduled to arrive at Dazhimen Station at 9:00 AM on the 12th, in order to allow all circles to greet them. The Welcoming Coffin Office also stipulated the order of welcoming the coffin, divided into nine groups: First group, bicycle team, national flag, mourning flag, pacification headquarters military band, 10th Army military police, garrison police, second group, provincial government military band, Pinghan Railway Bureau military police, boy scouts, President Li's portrait car, girl scouts, Mrs. Li Wu's portrait car, third group, garrison headquarters military band, Red Cross, Red Swastika Society, security association, fire brigade, representatives of wounded soldiers of the 1911 Revolution, fourth group, Wuhan schools, fifth group, 13th Division military band, foreign guests, general headquarters, pacification headquarters, Wuhan agencies affiliated with the provincial and municipal governments, guests from all walks of life, sixth group, representatives of charitable associations, representatives of various charitable halls, representatives of chambers of commerce and various industries, seventh group, representatives of the Huangpi Association, eighth group, water and electricity company band, comrades of the 1911 Revolution, ninth group, Li family, coffin. Wuhan agencies and organizations erected a total of thirty or forty 素坊 (decorated arches) to welcome the coffin and all lowered flags to mourn. Consulates of various countries stationed in Wuhan also flew flags at half-mast to show respect. According to Li Shaoji, the eldest son of Li, because the cemetery had not yet been selected, the coffin was temporarily placed in Hongshan, and a national funeral would be held at a later date. He himself would go to Tianjin after the coffin was temporarily placed to take care of everything. (April 11th)

Ancient Artifacts Continue to Be Discovered in Teng County 98

An Entire Stone Chamber from the Han Dynasty

The Interior Filled with Han Dynasty Images

Jinan Quick Communication: Shandong Province has repeatedly discovered ancient artifacts in recent years, especially Han Dynasty stone carvings. This time, a Zhou Dynasty tripod was discovered in Teng County. Wang Xiantang, the director of the Provincial Library, was ordered to investigate. While visiting the tomb of Cao Wang, he also discovered an entire stone chamber from the Han Dynasty and thousands of Han Dynasty stone carvings. Not only can the types and uses of Han Dynasty stone carvings be studied, but the architectural style of Han Dynasty palaces can also be referenced and researched. Moreover, the entire stone chamber from the Han Dynasty is unprecedented. The details are recorded as follows:

Wang Xiantang, the director of the Provincial Library, after investigating the ancient artifacts discovered in Anshang Village, Teng County, heard that there was a tomb of Cao Wang in the east of Anshang Village, which was an ancient site of Tengyi, so he went to investigate and unexpectedly discovered a stone chamber from the Han Dynasty. The interior contains Han Dynasty portraits, which are priceless. According to Wang Xiantang, the tomb of Cao Wang is located ten miles east of Anshang Village and resembles a small mountain. According to the locals, there are ninety-nine tombs on the mountain, but according to his investigation, only eight were found. The shape of the tombs is unspeakable. There is a square opening on the tomb that is level with the ground. Entering through the opening, one sees a stone chamber with walls on all four sides, each with a square door, forming a large room. Its depth may be visible to the edge, or its depth is unknown. All the stone slabs on the roof are supported by stone pillars. All the stone slabs in the tomb are Han Dynasty portraits, totaling more than a thousand pieces of various sizes. The height of the room is seven or eight feet, and the width is about ten feet. The wellhead has a stone cover with troughs and a nose in the middle for lifting. The coffins of the seventy-two martyrs of Luowenyu were transported to the rear for burial. (Photo by Central News Agency)

According to local legend, it is the tomb of Cao Cao's father, but according to his investigation, the interior contains Han Dynasty portraits, which proves that it was built by someone in the Han Dynasty to avoid the chaos. The stone chamber has an opening that is not a door, but a skylight of the stone chamber. Although eight have been discovered now, it is believed that there must be dozens, and the stone houses must be interconnected. It is a pity that they are buried by soil. As for the origin of the stone chamber, it is likely that during the late Han Dynasty, the world was in great chaos and wars raged everywhere. People at that time built this stone chamber to avoid the chaos. The reason for using stone is that the area from Anshang Village to the tomb of Cao Wang is all mountainous, making it easy to obtain stone. The poor built houses with stone, while the rich carved stone statues. The stone chamber discovered this time is complete from the Han Dynasty and has not been discovered in previous generations. Its value in cultural history is immeasurable. The value of the Han Dynasty portraits in the interior is even more significant. Although many Han Dynasty portraits have been discovered in the past, they are all fragments. It has not been possible to determine what kind of portraits were used on the walls and what kind were used on the pillars. After the discovery of this stone chamber, the types and uses of portraits can be determined. At the same time, the architectural style of Han Dynasty palaces can also be seen.

There are many portraits in the stone chamber, with varying degrees of carving refinement. The number of Han Dynasty stone carvings abandoned on the ground and on the mountain is countless. It is a pity that the villagers are ignorant and use them to build houses or temples and bridges, which is a great sigh. Seeing this situation, he has decided to collect and preserve them. The first step in preservation is to clear the mountain to investigate the exact number of wellheads (i.e., skylights of the stone chamber) and to open up the underground passages connecting the stone chambers, so that the entire stone chamber can be fully revealed, allowing people to enter and tour. Small pavilions will be built at the wellheads to protect them from wind and rain. The second step is to collect the Han Dynasty stone carvings scattered in various places and build a room to preserve them, so that people from all walks of life can visit and investigate. As for those that have already been used to build temples, bridges, and houses, they will be investigated one by one and ordered to be preserved forever. The above two matters will only cost several thousand yuan, but the ancient heritage can be permanently preserved. He has already drafted a budget and submitted it to the Provincial Government and the Department of Education for review. (April 11th)

Henan Public Works Bureau Actively Carries Out River Works 99

Supervisory Offices Established in Mengjin

Completion of Various Riverbed Dams and Embankments

Zhengzhou Communication: Since continuous years of disasters have left the people in dire straits, enthusiastic gentry have been running around appealing for urgent work relief and handling many projects. It is now heard that the Henan Provincial Public Works Bureau of the Engineering Department of the National Economic Commission will continue to handle the unfinished projects of last year's Flood Relief Committee in Zhengzhou. The largest and most important of these are the Mengjin Yellow River and Luoyang Luo River dam projects, as well as the Ying River bridge project and the Zhoukou Sha River embankment project. This project cost is 200,000 yuan allocated by the Engineering Department of the National Economic Commission for construction, with the remainder being raised separately by the local government to make up for the shortfall. The director of the bureau, Zhu Guangcai, has completed the planning and established supervisory offices in Tie Xie of Mengjin and Zhoukou, allocating engineering personnel to actively carry out the work. It is heard that the funds will arrive soon and work will begin immediately. This work achieves three good things at once, providing a livelihood for starving people, facilitating transportation, and preventing the water damage of the Yellow and Luo Rivers. The people of Henan are all rejoicing and looking forward to its success. (April 9th)

Another Kidnapping Case Occurs Near Tinglin 100

In Sidu, located about three miles east of Tinglin in Pudong, the Chen family, rural residents, were visited by many bandits on the evening of the 10th. Holding firearms, they broke into the main gate and looted at will. However, the Chen family was not wealthy and had no cash reserves, so the bandits kidnapped three members of the Chen family, both male and female, and escaped. It was reported to the First Sub-bureau of Public Security for rescue. By the time police officers arrived, the bandits had disappeared. The case has been reported to Songjiang, and orders have been given to investigate.

Jiading

Accidental Shooting of a Student While Cleaning a Gun 101

Wang Xingxian, a fifth-grade student at Huangdu Elementary School in Qingpu County and a native of Jiading, fifteen years old, was strolling downstream of the stage of the Huangdu Chenghuang Temple at around 4:00 PM on the 11th. Zhang Peishen, a member of the seventh squad of the third detachment of the police force, was cleaning his gun on the stage. Because he forgot to remove the bullet that was loaded in the gun the night before, he accidentally pulled the trigger, hitting the student, piercing his abdomen. The doctor at the village hospital washed and bandaged the wound, and he was sent to Shanghai for treatment by boat. He died midway due to the severity of the injury. Gao Baochen, the captain of the police force, immediately sent the police officer Zhang to the county government for punishment.

Tongsheng Pawnshop in Dongdai, Tongli Town, Wujiang County, suddenly caught fire at 3:00 AM on the 12th. The fire was very fierce. Because the local fire-fighting equipment was simple, it was impossible to put it out. It burned until about 6:00 AM, completely destroying all the buildings, six进 (sections), more than fifty rooms, and the items in pawn, with a loss of about 110,000 yuan. It is heard that the pawnshop has been open for more than 20 years, managed by Wang Boxuan, and the shareholders are汝孟,戴钱, Chun Sheng, etc. The cause of the fire is said to be that the pawnshop staff went out to watch a night show beforehand and left a cigarette butt in the cargo room when they returned. The local police station has now detained a司務 (clerk) from the pawnshop pending investigation.

Wujiang

Opposition to Enclosing Pangshan Lake 104

The Construction Committee中,将 (within), this county's Pangshan Lake is being enclosed to create an irrigation experimental field. Recently, workers have been hired to build dikes and banks. The nearby farmers, concerned about their livelihoods, gathered more than a thousand villagers from various villages and townships to petition in the city yesterday (the 10th) morning at 10:00 AM. The county's Public Security Bureau, fearing that the large number of people would cause trouble, prohibited traffic in the north gate. Later, Wang Zuxun, the head of the first district, came out of the city to explain that the petition should not cause disturbance. They then lined up and entered the city to petition the county government, all holding white flags with the words "Petition to Remove the Enclosure of Pangshan Lake" written on them. County Magistrate Wang came out to persuade them to return to their villages first and notified the workers to temporarily stop enclosing the area. The villagers were satisfied and returned to their villages separately.

Connecting Wuxi-Cheng Road with Shanghai-Nanjing Intermodal Transportation 106

Since the construction of the Wuxi-Cheng Highway, long-distance buses have been running, making transportation convenient. Recently, the Wuxi-Cheng Long-Distance Bus Company has formulated a plan to connect the Wuxi-Cheng Road with the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway for intermodal transportation. They are currently actively preparing and plan to contact the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Administration to sign a contract, which is expected to be implemented next month. However, the section of the road from Jiangyin West Gate to the riverside road is currently being developed by the county's Construction Bureau, but due to financial difficulties, the road surface has not yet been repaired, so it is not possible to run vehicles for the time being. Therefore, even ferry transportation cannot be realized, and the intercity bus between Huangtiangang Port and the southern outskirts is also difficult to become a reality.

Zhenjiang

Resolution of the Fuyun Steamer Dispute 107

The Fuyun Steamer Company in this port has been in a dispute with its workers due to unpaid wages. The Zhenjiang County Party Headquarters, together with the county government, convened representatives from the company's labor and management to talk and find a way to mediate. The final resolution is as follows: (1) The company will pay one month's wages to the long-term workers within one week, starting with the earliest unpaid months. In addition to the amount due for this month, another half-month's wages will be paid in order, but no later than June 10th. The remaining arrears will be repaid as soon as possible after the Zhen Qing class starts. (2) Starting this month, the company will pay all ship workers' wages at the end of each month without delay. (3) It is decided that the liquor expenses that the ship should receive should be handled according to the old practice. (4) The company shall not dismiss workers on the pretext of this wage claim.

Chinese Take Over the Suisheng Factory 108

The Suisheng Match Factory in Jinshanhe, this port, was originally founded by a Japanese named Ta Keno Takeo. In the spring of last year, the Japanese returned to his country, and the factory was shut down. So far, no one has taken it over. Recently, a wealthy merchant, Mr. Yang, has taken over the factory and renamed it the Neihe Trading Company. It has been greatly arranged in recent days, and the wholesale office has already started working. Men and women workers are signing up at the factory one after another, and the factory is scheduled to start operations on the first day of next month.
