Local News

The Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession Held Its General Assembly Yesterday 111

Xu Xinliu, Lin Kanghou and Others Were Elected as Chinese Committee Members

Chen Tingrui Was Elected as the Chinese Committee Member of the Land Committee

Hu Fengxiang and 27 Others Were Elected as Executive Committee Members

A Resolution Was Passed to Oppose the Municipal Council's Management of Factories, etc.

The first general assembly of the 12th session of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession was held yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM at the Bank Association Club at No. 4 Hong Kong Road. Xu Xinliu and four others were elected as Chinese directors to the Municipal Council for the 22nd year. Lin Lianhou and six others were elected as Chinese committee members. Chen Tingrui was elected as the Chinese committee member of the Land Committee. Hu Fengxiang and 27 others were elected as executive committee members of the association. Five important cases were also resolved. The details are recorded as follows:

Attending Representatives 112

Those who attended included Geng Jiaji, the representative of the Shanghai Municipal Government, Zhao Tiezhang, the section chief of the Diplomatic Ministry's Shanghai office, He Dekui, the secretary of the Municipal Council, and representatives of the association, Yu Qiaqing, Zhang Yichen, Fang Jiaobo, Qian Longzhang, Jiang Yiping, Wen Lanting, Shi Zhikun, Jin Runxiang, Cheng Xiechun, Chen Weiwen, Wang Hanliang, Shen Tianxin, Tao Yimin, Lin Kanghou, Li Bohan, Chu Huiseng, Yuan Ludeng, Cai Qiaojun, and more than seventy others.

Proceedings of the Meeting 113

At 2:30 PM, the meeting was opened with a bell. Yu Qiaqing was elected as chairman. The ceremony was performed as usual. First, the chairman gave a speech. Then, Yuan Ludeng, on behalf of all the directors and committee members, reported on the brief history of attending the Public Concession Municipal Council for the fifth session. Next, the chairman appointed four vote counters, Zhang Yichen, Wang Jian　, Hu Fengxiang, and Cheng Xiechun, and two vote callers, Yu Hualong and Cao Zhigong. They then separately elected the sixth session of directors and committee members attending the Municipal Council, land committee members, and executive committee members of the association. Then, proposals and temporary motions were discussed, and the meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM for tea and refreshments.

Chairman's Speech 114

Chairman Yu Qiaqing's speech stated: "Representatives of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, representatives of the municipal government, distinguished representatives, today is the first meeting of this year's congress. It is one day later than last year. When we slightly recall the situation at this time last year, we feel that the tranquility and prosperity of this port were of an unknown degree to which they would be damaged by the Japanese military. No observer could say for sure. However, in hindsight, we can be sure that without the bloody resistance of the Nineteenth Route Army and the Fifth Army, even the mediation of the representatives of the four countries, Britain, the United States, France, and Italy, would not have been enough to help achieve the May 5th ceasefire and troop withdrawal agreement and stabilize the current situation in Shanghai. However, when will the Japanese military be satisfied? We must not think that the places invaded and bombed by the Japanese military are far away in North China, and we can rest easy. We should know what the situation is north of the Suzhou River. In the year since the last congress, there have been many wars and alarms, and we have spared no effort. However, the Hongkou and Yangshupu areas, which were allowed to be used by the Japanese military as bases for aggressive military operations, even after the Municipal Council exempted three months, two months, or one and a half months of property taxes, and the landlords agreed to exempt rents, and the water and electricity companies slightly reduced usage fees, it is unknown when their economic vitality will recover. Even south of the Suzhou River, which was considered a relatively safe area at the time, only with a two-month shutdown, the purchasing power of the citizens of this city was insignificant, and the market gradually declined. Although there was still a lot of coming and going at the market, the sellers were stretched thin. Only shops are closing more and opening less. The closure of downtown areas and the turning over of properties to others are causing uncertainty, and it is unknown what will happen. Looking at the extent of the Japanese military's aggression, otherwise, the business of our Chinese people will not easily improve, and trade with various countries will inevitably decline day by day. This is enough to show that the Japanese military's aggression is enough to destroy world business. In the past year, what has made us concerned and regretful is the increase in telephone charges and the water problem. After the telephone was converted to automatic operation, its service has slightly improved, but the rash increase in prices is in fact incompatible with the post-war economy of society, and in theory, countless users must have suffered from the conversion project for two years, only bearing the cost but not being able to use it. Today, an automatic machine is installed, and tomorrow, there is an obligation to increase fees. Nothing is more unfair than this. Secondly, telephones in the road-building area beyond the boundary must also be converted to automatic machines within two years. This was originally stipulated in the contract, but the reason was that the draft contract was not approved, and the work could not be completed within the stipulated period. The Shanghai Telephone Company was allowed by the Public Concession Bureau to waive its obligation to perform, and the user's financial difficulties and requests not to increase prices immediately were all deemed to be due to the contractual relationship, and it was inevitable. Moreover, the company's miscalculation and excessive expansion, resulting in the inability to distribute dividends, was also considered a reason for the need to increase prices. What is even more painful for the global legal community is the retroactive charging of fees, which destroys the legal principle of 'no retroactivity' by the people of the rule of law. It can be seen that where there is profit, they are unwilling to do anything. Fortunately, telephones are not something that people cannot live without for a day, so even if they are resolutely removed, there is no major harm. However, this is not the case with tap water. According to the tap water in the Public Concession, it has been around for forty or fifty years. Its charging method, like the municipal general donation, is based on rent as the standard, that is, 5% of the rent is collected every month as water charges. In the simple procedures, it contains social policies that alleviate social economy. About six or seven years ago, it was increased to 6%. In March of the 17th year of the Republic of China, when the Chinese directors were about to join the Municipal Council, a new contract was signed, changing the previous method and allowing an interest guarantee of 9%, 8%, and 7%, but still using gold pounds as the capital unit. As a result, the exchange rate fell, resulting in an insufficient amount of silver exchanged for gold to pay the pound interest, and a surcharge of one-quarter was added. For a time, refusal to pay and cutting off water caused a huge storm. The reasons for the dispute have long been reported. Unexpectedly, the Hill report was not fully implemented, and the contract for water meters was not studied in detail for methods of controlling waste. There was no scientific experiment on how much the water fee should be. It was rashly assumed that the original five jiao per thousand gallons of silver dollars plus a surcharge of 0.25 was 0.625 jiao as the basic price of the water fee. As a result, the water fee calculated by the meter was several times higher than before, and some even exceeded the rent. The declaration that 'installing a meter to control waste does not increase the price' has almost become inversely proportional, and fundamentally conflicts with the principle of the Hill report that installing a meter to calculate fees does not increase the burden on the poor and small households. However, the water company does not immediately give discounts to those who fully pay according to the meter, such as the Wing On Textile Factory Company. For a time, the landlords who collected and remitted water fees successively made a fuss and refused to sign the water meter contract, threatening to cut off the water. It goes without saying that those who refuse to pay will naturally be forced to cut off the water. More than 30 users have had their water cut off, and the number of citizens who have been cut off from cooking and drinking is numerous, and their situation is very pitiful. I don’t know how many people were intimidated by the threat of water cutoffs and paid the fees. Seeing that the situation was not being straightened out by the world, the water company asked the Municipal Council to allow a discount of at least one-third of the previous water fee. If so, installing a water meter would require an additional one-third of the water fee. However, the Wing On Company was able to recover some of the fees it had paid according to the meter after questioning, which can be said to be a good thing in misfortune. After this large-scale water cutoff, and fearing that the victims would defend themselves according to the law, the Chinese and Western detectives hired by the taxpayers' donations were specially used to suppress the scene, even though the citizens with a traditional spirit of peace were targeted. In the end, an incident that was bound to happen in a civilized country was not caused. However, under the circumstances that the public's anger was difficult to violate and the desire for exclusivity was difficult to achieve, the original water contract was shelved, and another trial method was set, which has been implemented on April 1. It is said that there is also an advisory committee dedicated to the matter. Although the handling is still considered too late, we are very impressed by the attitude of the parties involved in changing their minds. At the same time, we have to express our gratification in two things, one is education and the other is defense. Regarding the education problem, this association exchanged documents with the Municipal Council on March 26 of the 17th year of the Republic of China, specifically stipulating concrete provisions. Now, all four Chinese children's public schools have Chinese vice-principals, and five primary schools have been established. Although it does not conform to the defense method of adding two schools every year according to the eight-year plan, it is indeed a fact that it is gradually progressing. However, from our point of view, education is a major plan for cultivating talents for a hundred years, and the construction of school buildings must also be consolidated. However, it seems too large to require approximately 700,000 yuan for a small school building. It is better to only seek perfunctoriness in terms of construction, so the cost of two schools can be used to build three schools, which can educate more younger brothers and sisters, and further reduce the number of out-of-school children in the concession to increase the intelligence of citizens. Two girls' middle schools were originally planned, and one has already been opened, with many students. In addition, there was a provision for 150,000 taels of subsidy school fees established by the association the year before, which was proportional to donations. Chinese schools can get 55% of them, but due to various rent obstacles, they were only able to distribute them last year. This year's is also increased compared to the previous year. Although it is far from the provision in the above-mentioned exchange of documents that education expenses should account for 20% of the total expenditure, the Municipal Council has paid attention to citizen education, which should be appreciated. Regarding defense issues, in the past year, the expenses have been 80 times higher than in the first year of the Republic of China, and the strict handling of criminal cases has indeed been more advanced than in the previous year. The detection of kidnapping cases and the rescue of hostages have been rapid and resourceful, which is admirable. The association once sent a letter to the Municipal Council to commend the people who made the effort. However, we believe that the commission of a crime requires many factors, but the initiators must not be very numerous. Among them, those who are unemployed and forced to be cold and forced to join the gang account for the majority. If there is a way to give these coerced people work education, it will be a radical method to reduce crime, and to extract a part of the amount from the defense fee to handle this matter is something that taxpayers and municipal experts believe should be done. The active elimination of crime is no less than the passive suppression, and the great achievement of public security can be achieved. However, representatives, the 950,000 or more citizens we represent, who represent more than 96% of the population in the concession, will have a serious problem to be solved at present or at the latest next year. What is the problem? According to the current financial method and the declining market situation, the income of the Municipal Council will definitely not be enough to meet the expenditure next year. We deeply know that the municipal institution is a permanent organization of citizens. Citizens have new and old representatives, and this institution is actually a potential extension. Individual expenditures must be based on income as the standard, while those who manage municipal affairs often ignore the general economy of society, and always expand the annual budget to show the gradual upward trend of prosperity. Some even regard it as face. In fact, before the World War, politicians and economists generally felt this way, which led to the great reaction of the party and even the implementation. As Mr. MacDonald, the British Prime Minister, said at the closing of the Lausanne Conference on July 9 last year, "The prosperity of the public depends on the prosperity of each individual." He even destroyed the world by saying that the British budget was not enough to meet the needs, and the annual cost was thousands of castings. Many professors and economic experts from the University of Chicago wrote to the US President on January 21 this year, advocating that the US budget does not need to be balanced under the current economic conditions. A fake balanced budget is just a habit. This kind of opinion is very noteworthy and can be an important reference for us. That is, US President Roosevelt issued an executive order on March 28 this year, reducing the salaries of federal government officials by 15%, and the President, Supreme Court judges, and members of Congress are no exception. At the same time, the army, navy, and air force must also reduce their salaries. This kind of action, at least the economic bankruptcy of the city of Chicago, is also one of its lessons. However, has our Municipal Council been affected by the global economic downturn? Has it been affected by the Shanghai War? Has it been affected by the general economic decline of society? All senior officials have not seen a reduction in salaries when the exchange rate is high, but when the exchange rate is low, they are given an exchange loss subsidy of 1.45 million yuan a year, and the increase in salaries and endowments is still the same. The taxpayers who are affected by the economic downturn have to pay everything to meet the needs. Representatives, we must not say that the land donation and the house donation are still 0.7% and 14%, respectively. We must know that the rate has not changed, but the tax has increased. The land donation is increased by estimating high land prices, and the house donation is increased by rising rents. This year's land price has also been overestimated, and the rents are about to be destroyed. It is really a good method to take rent as the standard, but to carry out high estimation calculation. We must pay close attention to and supervise this kind of dark handling method. Our proposition is not that we do not love the Municipal Council, but that we love the Municipal Council very much. It is to maintain the principle that donations and taxes do not hurt the tax source and cultivate the tax source, so that the market, which is on the verge of desperation, will no longer decline and will have the hope of recovery, so that vacant houses will be rented by people, either as shops or as residences, to increase the income of the municipal general donation of the Municipal Council, so that the budget will not become a written expression. As for the continuous increase in land prices, which indirectly leads to further increases in rents, this must be paid special attention to. For example, the editorial of the Shanghai Times on March 29 this year stated that the budget makers should aim at invariance and standardization, and the comment of Mr. Hu Dehai of the Great American Evening News on March 30 stated at the end that Shanghai is still affected by last year's war and must continue to adopt austerity measures before the market shows signs of recovery. The Great American Evening News also published several editorials, hoping that the Municipal Council's annual budget will be announced earlier, which is what we agree with. The addition of Chinese members to the Land Committee, after more than a year of consultation, has been satisfactorily resolved, which further shows the practical cooperation of the taxpayers in this district and is extremely gratifying. We are even more grateful for the efforts of the Chinese directors and committee members to seek benefits for our taxpayers."

Report of the Directors and Committee Members 115

The report of Dong and Committee Members Yu Qiaqing and Yuan Ludeng who attended the Public Concession Bureau in the fifth session stated: "The hardships experienced by the people of Shanghai in the 21st year of the Republic of China are unprecedented in history. When we were elected by the previous congress as directors and committee members of the Public Concession Bureau, it was just after the end of the war and the devastation had not yet recovered. The Zhabei area was devastated and the casualties were relatively high. Therefore, the initial administration in the bureau was anxious to stabilize the local area and comfort the refugees. The recovery of municipal power in the war zone, the relief of the affected merchants and people, and the prevention of epidemics in the war zone were all carried out in order. After the local security was initially stabilized and order was gradually restored, the various routine construction matters of the municipal administration were discussed, weighed their importance, and distinguished their order. Now that the term of office has expired, we respectfully report to the representatives on the major policies implemented by the Municipal Council in the past year. (1) Distribution of seats on the Administrative Committee. An Administrative Committee is established under the Board of Directors of the Municipal Council. Its number has increased or decreased over the years. This year's committee is not much different from last year. There are more than 40 Chinese members who have the right to participate in various administrative matters in the bureau. The Chinese School Subsidy Committee is purely organized by Chinese people. In addition to the School Affairs Committee, which holds a meeting once every two weeks, the meeting schedule of other committees depends on the simplicity of the affairs. The names and personnel of the main committees are listed below: Finance Committee, 6 members, 2 Chinese members, Director Xu Xinliu and Committee Member Bei Songsun; School Affairs Committee, 7 members, 4 Chinese members, Director Yuan Ludeng, Committee Member Lin Kanghou, and President Liu Zhanen of Shanghai University and Vice President Ou Yuanhuai of Great China University; Police Committee, 7 members, 3 Chinese members, Director Yu Qiaqing, Hu Mengjia, and Committee Member Chen Tingrui; Public Works Committee, 6 members, 2 Chinese members, Director Yuan Ludeng and Committee Member Guo Shun; Public Utilities Committee, 5 members, 2 Chinese members, Director Hu Mengjia and Committee Member Wu Yunzhai; Employees Committee, 6 members, 2 Chinese members, Director Liu Hongsheng and Committee Member Guo Shun; Health Committee, 7 members, 3 Chinese members, Director Liu Hongsheng, Committee Member Long Zhang, and Doctor Kuang Fengtie; Transportation Committee, 6 members, 2 Chinese members, Committee Members Wu Yunzhai and Chen Tingrui; Music Committee, 4 members, 1 Chinese member, Huang Jinwu, Director of Academic Affairs of the National Conservatory of Music; Rent Arbitration Committee, 5 members, 1 Chinese member, Kui Yanfang, Manager of the Real Estate Trust Department of Zhejiang Xingye Bank; Library Committee, 6 members, Chinese members, Director Xu Xinliu and Wang Yunwu, Manager of the Commercial Press. (2) Post-War Reconstruction Facilities in Shanghai. The Shanghai War lasted for a month, and its tragedy should still be in the memory of the citizens. The Public Concession declared martial law on January 28 last year, and local order did not return to its pre-war state until June 13. The Municipal Council specifically adopted donation exemption measures to relieve the affected merchants and people. The northern and eastern districts were the most severely affected, and the amount of exemption ranged from three months, two months, to one and a half months. Other special treatments were handled separately according to their respective circumstances. After the outbreak of the war, the people in the affected areas gathered within the concession. Excluding those who lived in the homes of relatives and friends, public organizations tried to accommodate them. By the end of February, the number reached 70,000, mostly women and children. By the end of March, it had decreased to 53,470, and by the end of April, it was 19,705. By the end of May, only 400 people remained. Those in the Hongkou and North Sichuan Road areas who could not escape were rescued by the committees specially established by the public organizations and the Municipal Council. There were a total of 85 refugee shelters and 26 temporary hospitals, all of which were tax-exempt. With the cooperation of various organizations and shipping companies, most of the refugees were able to leave Shanghai one after another, and the congestion in the concession was cleared before the summer. As for those who lost their jobs due to the war, there were 160,000 in the concession alone by the end of February. If family members are added, the number would reach 500,000. By the end of May, most of the factories had resumed work, and the number had decreased to 45,000. Some Chinese factories also paid living expenses during the shutdown period. The epidemic prevention work began on March 14. The entire war zone was divided into three districts. The average amount of garbage and filth swept by the team every day was 15 tons. More than 100,000 people were vaccinated. The daily cost was 5,000 taels. It was not cleared until mid-June. Therefore, even after the war, the summer epidemic was not worse than in previous years. (3) Progress in Chinese Education. The most notable progress in Chinese education this year was three: (1) Subsidizing private schools. The Municipal Council and the Municipal Education Bureau agreed on cooperation methods for subsidy fees. All Chinese private schools in the concession, whether registered with the Education Bureau or not, but allowed to try out, can be subsidized by the Education Bureau on behalf of the Municipal Council. A total of 57 schools were subsidized throughout the year, with a total subsidy of 80,000 taels of silver. The largest was an annual subsidy of 14,000 taels, paid in four seasons. In addition, the Chinese Education Office and the Health Office sent staff to inspect and determine their use according to their needs. In 1933, the number of schools requesting subsidies increased by 30, so the amount set in the budget also increased to 100,000 taels, which is more than before. (2) Establishment of new schools. The two primary school buildings in the western and eastern districts have been completed and will be moved into one after another. In addition, a primary school was opened at the former China Merchants Public School site leased on Huade Road to meet the needs. The number of students reached more than 600. In addition, there was an original primary school building on Huishan Road. It was originally planned to be used for other purposes when the new school building on Jingzhou Road was completed. Now the original plan has been discarded, and it will still be used for running a primary school. There are now five Chinese primary schools in the concession. Except for one on Huade Road and one on Huishan Road, which are still rented civilian houses, the others have their own school buildings. The foundation is solid, and the development is rapid. As for girls' middle schools, the number of students is developing very well. The purchase of land for building a school building is already in the plan. (3) Improvement of the old system. Senior faculty members of the four Chinese Children's Public Schools are mostly Westerners. This year, each school has added one Chinese vice-principal to be responsible for presiding over the Chinese curriculum and allocating teaching responsibilities. The curriculum has also been improved to suit the current school system. A scholarship has also been established, with 10 places. Students who have passed the entrance examination from the bureau-established primary school and other schools will be rewarded for their outstanding achievements. (4) Return of Road Construction Beyond the Boundary. The negotiations on road construction beyond the boundary have been heard outside. The specific methods have not yet been negotiated. The foreign directors all have a unanimous desire to resolve this issue as soon as possible. It is our duty to expedite its completion. According to the area beyond the boundary, the scope is quite wide. The unfortunate incident last year occurred there. It should be properly planned to return it remotely so that all disputes, such as the construction of roadbeds and the operation of public utilities, can be swept away, which is what local people are happy to hear. It is an act of recovering legal rights, and its significance is even more significant. (5) Negotiations on Water Meter Issues. There is nothing wrong with installing water meters to prevent waste. It has been used in major cities in Europe and the West for a long time. However, due to the habit of the Public Concession over the years, the water fee is paid by the landlord on behalf of the tenant. After trying the water meter, the water fee increased sharply, and some were even nine times higher than the original fee. As a result, the rental income was only enough to pay the water fee, which was still not enough. The Real Estate Association came forward to protest. Some landlords refused to pay the water fee. The Shanghai Water Company threatened to cut off the water. For a time, the two sides were deadlocked, and the situation was very tense. The Board of Directors of the Municipal Council held repeated meetings to properly plan a solution. After several mediations and guarantees, the Municipal Council, the Water Company, and Mr. Feng Bingnan discussed a fair charging method for installing water meters so that after implementation, poor users would not be burdened, and landlords would not have additional expenses. Now, Mr. Feng's suggestion has been adopted. First, a trial period will be set, and the necessary water consumption of each grade of users will be estimated. During the trial period, fees will be charged according to this amount. For those with higher rents, the water fee will be slightly higher than the current water meter system. The rate will gradually decrease according to the amount of rent. For those with very low rents, the rate will be lower than the current price. This method has been implemented on April 1 and published in various newspapers. The trial period is temporarily set for one year, and then the water meter charging system will be formulated according to the experience gained so that it can be adapted to local conditions and implemented without obstruction. (6) Increase of Land Committee Members. The Land Committee established by the Municipal Council in accordance with the Land Regulations to handle disputes over the acquisition of private land intends to add two Chinese members. An agreement was reached last year, and the Chinese and Western Taxpayers' Congress passed a motion authorizing the Municipal Council to contact the relevant authorities and handle the procedures for increasing Chinese directors. The Municipal Council originally requested the right to agree on candidates. After negotiations, it has been abandoned. Now all the procedures have been completed. It is expected that two people will be elected, one by the Chinese Real Estate Association to represent the legal interests of the landlords, and the other by the Taxpayer's Association to represent the legal interests of the taxpayers. It is necessary to ensure that the public interest and private interests are balanced and there is no bias or lightness. In addition to respecting private rights, the intention of preserving the public interest is also preserved. (7) Maintenance of Budget Balance. In recent years, due to the high price of gold and the development of the municipal administration, the expenses of the Municipal Council have increased day by day. There have been proposals to increase donations, but they have been repeatedly delayed because of the consideration of the decline of the market and the depletion of the people's resources. Increasing the burden is contrary to economic principles. The 1933 budget has been compiled, and the shortfall is 1.42 million taels of silver, which is equal to the income of 2.9 months of general donations. According to the budgets of previous years, there were surpluses, but last year there was a deficit, but the amount was very small, only more than 50,000 taels. If the deficit is as large as this year, it is unprecedented. Although various administrative departments have made efforts to tighten their belts, development plans that require too much money have been shelved, and it is still difficult to maintain the balance of income and expenditure. Fortunately, after the sale of the Electricity Department, the bureau has a large amount of money to inject. It has now been decided to allocate 1.5 million taels from the sale account to make up for the budget shortfall. The increase in donations can be delayed. After the war last year, people's lives were difficult, and the local vitality has not yet recovered. Therefore, this move is also required by the environment. The above seven matters may be known to you or not. They are all important policies implemented by the Municipal Council this year and are closely related to the welfare of our Chinese citizens. According to the regulations, each administrative department in the bureau has a monthly report and an annual report to make the administrative situation public to the citizens. The reason is that the citizens are the main body of the local area, and they should be informed of the quality of the municipal facilities and supervise them. The aforementioned monthly reports are published in the Municipal Council's distribution reports and various newspapers every month. The annual report is compiled into a book, both in Chinese and English, and published for circulation. The administrative details of this year have been registered and can be reviewed at any time. We have been entrusted with the responsibility of the Chinese taxpayers, and we have made every effort to fulfill all the local welfare-related and legal rights. We are still ashamed that we have not been able to live up to the expectations of the society and the encouragement of you. I hope you can understand this. Reported by Yu Qiaoliao, Yuan Ludeng, Xu Xinliu, Liu Hongsheng, Hu Mengjia, Lin Kanghou, Chen Yinrui, Wu Yunxian, Bei Songsun, Guo Shun."

Resolutions Passed 120

The various important proposals were discussed and resolved by the general assembly as follows: (1) The proposal regarding the Municipal Council managing factories. Explanation: The Shanghai Municipal Council will hold a special meeting of taxpayers at 5 PM on April 19th, during which the fourth proposal will be presented: "Please amend clause 34 of the Land Regulations appendix, that is,"

"In the first line of the clause, after the words 'within this boundary,' add the words 'owning or occupying, opening a factory or workshop, or engaging in industry.'" Resolution: According to the opinion of this general assembly, most of the factories in the International Settlement employ Chinese workers. If factory management laws are established separately from the Chinese government and Chinese factory laws, it would be detrimental to China's sovereignty. Therefore, it is specifically resolved that any proposal or amendment to the Land Regulations and attached laws that would grant the Municipal Council the power to manage, inspect, or supervise all factories within the settlement should not be agreed to. Proposal to add a Chinese auditor to the Municipal Council. Explanation: Article 12 of the Shanghai Foreign Settlement Regulations stipulates that all income and expenditure accounts managed by the directors should be audited, and the audit situation should be publicly announced after being approved by the taxpayers' meeting. This meeting should be held when consuls of various countries convene an annual meeting. Resolution: According to the opinion of this general assembly, in order to satisfy the wishes of our Chinese citizens and adapt to the needs of the environment, it is necessary for the Shanghai International Settlement Municipal Council to hire qualified Chinese individuals to audit the accounts. The Municipal Council is hereby authorized to proceed with all necessary procedures in order to realize the hiring of one Chinese auditor as soon as possible. Also, a temporary proposal: (1) Jin Runxiang proposed that all taxpayers within the settlement, regardless of whether they are Chinese or foreign, should hold a joint taxpayers' meeting. Resolution: To be studied in detail by the executive committee. (2) Hu Fengxiang proposed that senior Chinese staff should be rapidly increased in important departments of the Municipal Council, such as the police department, fire department, and health department, in order to eliminate barriers. Resolution: Approved in principle and handed over to the executive committee for handling. (3) Liu Zhongying proposed that the Municipal Council should pay attention to relieving unemployment. Resolution: Handed over to the executive committee for research and implementation of specific plans.

Shanghai Commemorates the Purge Yesterday 124

The Municipal Party Headquarters Held a Commemorative Meeting in the Morning

The Chinese and Foreign Authorities Strengthened Defenses

Yesterday was the sixth anniversary of the Chinese Nationalist Party's purge. The local Municipal Party Headquarters convened representatives from various agencies and organizations at 10:00 AM in the party headquarters to hold a commemorative ceremony, which adjourned at 11:00 AM. At the same time, it was also a commemoration of the "April 12th" communists, so the defenses in the local area were also strengthened compared to usual. The following is a record of the events:

The Municipal Party Headquarters Holds a Commemorative Meeting 125

Yesterday at 10:00 AM, the Municipal Party Headquarters held a commemorative meeting in the auditorium on the third floor of the headquarters on Linyin Road. More than a hundred representatives from the municipal government, the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Municipal Farmers' Association, and various district party headquarters, labor unions, and schools attended the meeting. After the meeting began, Tong Xingbai, Chairman of the Party Headquarters Executive Committee, and Tong Muge, Master of Ceremonies, performed the ceremonies as required. First, Chairman Tong gave a speech, stating that today is the first day of the party's purge movement that began six years ago. Regarding the significance of this purge movement, I believe everyone understands it. When the purge was implemented in the sixteenth year of the Republic, it caused doubt among many people, because there was first tolerance of the communists, and then a purge occurred. The policy of the Nationalist Party seems to have contradictions. However, it is actually quite easy to understand this. At that time, the tolerance of the communists was in the hope that the Communist Party could truly engage in revolution. However, since the tolerance of the communists in the thirteenth year of the Republic until the sixteenth year, it was not only discovered that the Communist Party could not engage in revolution, but the Communist Party also provoked discord and always harbored the intention of disrupting and subverting the party. The Nationalist Party had to take purge actions because of this. Therefore, it is not that the Communist Party cannot be tolerated, but that after tolerance, the Communist Party did not strive for revolution, but instead had a conspiracy to rebel. This is a contradiction of the Communist Party, not a contradiction of the Nationalist Party. As for the Communist Party's political struggles in various countries, they exist in various European countries, which is well known to anyone. However, looking back at the communist parties in various countries, none of them are like the ones in China, who specialize in murder and arson. Take the past in this city as an example. Whenever there is a communist memorial day, the communists secretly distribute meaningless leaflets and slightly damage a few tram windows, which can be their direct action, returning reports to their superiors to claim credit. Consider whether this policy can succeed. Recently, many people in China have surrendered. We only need to ask them how the internal work of the Communist Party is, and we will know that what I said is not false. Also, at this time of national crisis and deepening foreign troubles, the Communist Party is still jumping around in the rear. Therefore, the Nationalist Party's purge in the past was first of all to unite and unify the party's forces. But from another perspective, it is to eliminate the Communist disaster so that we can eliminate foreign troubles and achieve true success. Therefore, the significance of the Nationalist Party's purge is to hope that comrades within the party will jointly bear this responsibility, work together, and achieve the goal of clearing the communists before we can save the country. Then, slogans were shouted and the meeting adjourned.

Chinese and Foreign Authorities Strengthen Defenses 126

Yesterday was the anniversary of the Nationalist Party's purge movement, and at the same time, it was the Communist Party's "April 12th" anniversary. In order to prevent the Communist Party from causing trouble, the military and police authorities in this city strengthened precautions. Starting at 7:00 AM, the entire Public Security Bureau was dispatched, and double sentries were added at major intersections and important passes. The old Ximen Li Bin Bridge, the north and south train station direction offices, and the special arrest teams were stationed to check suspicious pedestrians. The public and French concession authorities also took extremely strict precautions. Police cars patrolled the remote sections of the Western Shanghai area bordering the Chinese-controlled areas from time to time. Because the precautions were extremely tight, there were no disturbances throughout the day.

The National Lawyers Association Sends a Telegram to the U.S. President to Pay Attention to the Sino-Japanese Issue 127

The National Lawyers Association yesterday sent a telegram to the U.S. President and also sent telegrams to legal groups nationwide, stating, "For reference by newspaper offices and legal groups: Recently, it was read in the newspapers that U.S. President Roosevelt invited representatives from various countries to go to Washington to exchange opinions on the revitalization of the world economy. It is the opinion of this association that the revitalization of the world economy is closely and inseparably related to world peace and order. A telegram is specifically sent to President Roosevelt, with the text: Washington, Chinese Minister Shi Zhaoji, please forward to His Excellency President Roosevelt: The prosperity of the world economy must be built on the foundation of world peace and order. Now, when the violent Japan is destroying peace in the Far East, we are delighted to meet His Excellency the President's grand event of inviting representatives from various countries to exchange opinions on the revitalization of the world economy. This association expresses its deep sympathy and hopes to promote the spirit of the Non-Aggression Pact and the Nine-Power Treaty to eliminate the factors that disrupt world peace, so that economic revitalization can be as easy as turning one's hand. Otherwise, the world's largest market will be trampled on, gradually occupied exclusively by the strong, and further increase the flames of its threat to the world. In this way, not only will there be no hope for the world economy to recover, but we worry about the future and dare to ask the world. We hope for a bright future. The matter concerns the happiness of all mankind and not only the interests of the Far East. We hope for unanimous support and are extremely eager. Liu Liumin, Jiang Yong, Yan Yinwu, Dai Tianqiu, Liu Zhe, Standing Committee Members of the All-China Lawyers Association, respectfully."

New Director of the Mint, Lu Xuepu, Assumed Office Yesterday 129

The Entire Factory Remained as Before, with No Personnel Changes

Increase the Number of Coins Minted to Meet Needs

The resignation of Guo Chengen, Director of the Central Mint, was approved. The Executive Yuan's meeting the day before resolved to appoint Lu Xuepu as his successor. Mr. Lu arrived at the factory at 9:00 AM yesterday to take over. The details are recorded below:

Assumed Office Yesterday Morning 130

Mr. Lu arrived at the factory at 9:00 AM. The former director, Mr. Guo Chengen, was waiting at the factory to hand over the office. Because there were no changes in the staff of each department, the procedures were very simple. Former Director Guo gathered all the factory staff in the auditorium, introduced the new director, and urged all the staff to do their best to help the new director complete the factory's mission in sorting out the currency system. Then Director Lu gave a speech and the meeting dispersed. The ceremony was very simple.

Director Lu's Instructions 131

Lu Xuepu gave instructions to all the factory staff, saying, "This factory began to be established in the ninth year of the Republic. At that time, I was serving in the Ministry of Finance in Beiping, preparing everything, and I also participated in it. It has been operating for more than ten years and has a rough scale. The times have changed, and I have not been able to see it completed. Since Director Guo took office, he has actively engaged in minting work. After the news of the opening on March 1st spread, all sectors admired his extraordinary perseverance. This is the only commemoration of this factory, which is admired by us. Director Guo has formulated a number of preferential regulations for all employees, such as savings, insurance, and pensions, etc., on the one hand, to stabilize the lives of all employees, and on the other hand, to stimulate the sense of responsibility of all employees."

The Jiangnan Railway Company is Scheduled to Hold an Inaugural Meeting in Shanghai 132

Acceptance of the Ningxiang Property Approved by the Ministry of Railways

Laying the Wuhu-Zhapu Railway Will Commence Shortly

The Jiangnan Railway Company has been preparing for more than six months. The fixed capital of one million yuan has now been fully raised and has been largely paid. Surveying plans, land acquisition, and material procurement have also been completed. It is now learned that the company is scheduled to convene shareholders on the 19th of this month to hold an inaugural meeting to formally establish the company, and it plans to start construction at the end of this month, in order to complete the project and open it to traffic as soon as possible. The following is an exploration of the progress of the preparations:

Surveying Work 133

The Jiangnan Railway Industrial Division operates the railway transportation business, selecting the Wuhu to Zhapu route, laying railways in stages. The first phase will first build from Wuhu to Sunjiabu. The surveying work began on August 21 of this year. By October 6, the Wuhu to Xuancheng section was surveyed and completed. This section uses a portion of the old Ningxiang Railway line, measuring 67.7 kilometers. After the completion of the Su-Xuancheng section, various materials and standard charts were actively prepared, and the surveying work from Xuancheng to Sunjiabu was completed. As for the Taozhi to Xuancheng section, the acquisition of the roadbed has now been submitted to the provincial government for requisition in accordance with the Land Acquisition Law, and roadbed earthwork is currently under construction.

Extending the Route 134

The company's plan originally scheduled the first phase of construction to be from Wuhu to Xuancheng, totaling 67.7 kilometers, with a budget of 1.69 million yuan (excluding the Ningxiang line property of the Ministry of Railways). Now, after detailed estimation by Engineer Hong, if the most economical construction method is used, the route extended to Sunjiabu Town in the southeast of Xuancheng may not exceed the original budget. It is found that Sunjiabu is an important grain-producing town in southern Anhui, and the population and commerce are more prosperous than Wanzhi. It is also the place through which the coal mine railway of Shuidong passes. In the future, it will be a fixed transport route for rice, grain, coal and wood, so extending the route is a very good idea.

Filing for Registration 135

The surveying charts of the Wuhu-Xuancheng section were sent to Nanjing at the end of last October, and a document was immediately prepared and sent to the Ministry of Railways requesting registration. Zhang Renjie, Chairman of the Preparatory Committee, personally contacted Minister Gu several times to achieve a satisfactory solution. At that time, the Ministry of Railways proposed joint operations with the company and the use of heavy rails, but the difficulties were explained in detail and could not be followed. Provisional registration was approved, and the approval was not received until December 5th. The license was not issued until January of this year.

Transfer of Property 136

Since the company has selected a portion of the old Ningxiang Railway line, it has negotiated with the Ministry of Railways on the transfer of the old Ningxiang base, Wuhu-Wanzhi section, property of the Ministry for a permanent solution. This section of the base was built early and has three railway bridges, but it was stopped due to some reason and the rails were not laid. According to the estimate of Mr. Gruf, the chief engineer sent by the Ministry of Communications in the fifth year of the Republic, the value of this property is 720,000 yuan. However, seventeen years have passed, and the railway bridge earthwork must have been damaged, so Zhang Renjie and Minister Gu agreed that the company and the Ministry of Railways would sign a contract to transfer the property, valued at 360,000 yuan. Repayments will begin on December 1, 1929, with an annual interest rate of 6%. Except for the last half year, each half year will repay 28,000 yuan in principal and interest, and the full amount will be repaid in seven and a half years. After thirty years, the Ministry of Railways will continue to buy it back at a price. The contract has been signed by the company and sent to the ministry. However, in order to protect the future construction of the Ningxiang Railway, the Ministry of Railways has exchanged documents with the company, stating that the Ministry of Railways has the right to build a parallel railway from Wuhu to Wanzhi. The company has already agreed to this matter.

Date of Commencement 137

The company's preparations are all in order, and it has purchased many cars and freight cars from the Beining Railway Bureau. Other materials have also been processed, so it is urgent to start construction in order to open to traffic as soon as possible. It is now learned that the company is scheduled to hold a foundation laying ceremony in Wuhu before the end of this month to start construction.

Inaugural Meeting 138

Cheng Qilu's Report 143

The Experience of the Fierce Battle at Lengkou

Shang Zhen's representative, Cheng Qilu, reported to the Shanghai Public Associations on the process of annihilating the enemy at Lengkou, saying, "Qilu was ordered by General Commander Shang Qizi to come to Shanghai. His mission is twofold: first, to convey the deep gratitude of the Commander and all officers and soldiers of the Corps to the various Shanghai groups for the supplies received through General Zhu Ziqiao. Second, concerning the Battle of Lengkou, gentlemen in Shanghai concerned about national affairs have sent letters and telegrams inquiring about the battle situation. At that time, the replies were brief and not exhaustive. Now that the enemy's offensive has been defeated and the defenses have become more consolidated, I have been instructed to make a more detailed report to you. Qilu is not eloquent, so I will present a brief outline: (1) Recapturing Lengkou: Our Corps' defense was originally focused on the Luan River area. The Lengkou area was originally under the defense of another army. However, since the loss of Rehe, Lengkou was also occupied by the enemy on the evening of the 4th of last month. Upon receiving the report, our army, recognizing the importance of the pass, which not only affected our flank but also the safety of Pingjin, immediately dispatched the Huang Guanghua Division to block the enemy. The division set out that night, advancing at full speed, and arrived at Huan'an on the evening of the 5th. Initially, the enemy only had over two hundred Japanese soldiers and over ten armored vehicles. On the 4th and 5th, the enemy gradually increased to over a thousand soldiers, with sixty or seventy armored vehicles and tanks, mixed with puppet troops, infantry, and artillery, and constructed fortifications to try to hold the pass. On the evening of the 6th, Huang Division's Jiang Regiment advanced towards Jianchangying and launched a night attack on Lengkou. Before dawn on the 7th, they began attacking the enemy's position. The enemy stubbornly resisted, relying on the terrain. Our infantry and artillery fired together, destroying dozens of enemy vehicles. The enemy suffered heavy casualties. Until 5 p.m. that afternoon, the enemy could not withstand the assault and retreated north in disarray. We used a main force to hold Lengkou and sent another force to pursue the enemy. Corpses littered the road, and the enemy suffered heavy losses. We captured many enemy artillery shells, rifles, orders, maps, and other items. (2) Lengkou's Defense and Equipment: After recovering Lengkou, we anticipated that the enemy would value the pass and launch a counterattack. We had to urgently devise defensive measures. However, the area is mountainous, and materials were scarce, making construction difficult. Therefore, we decided to deploy troops outside the pass to annihilate the enemy by opportunity, preventing them from approaching the Great Wall. (3) The Enemy's Second Counterattack: On the 17th and 18th of last month, a large number of enemies were discovered in the Dushan area, and a fierce battle was anticipated. On the 19th, dozens of enemy cavalry engaged with the plainclothes team led by platoon leader Zhenying of the Cai Lin Regiment at Jianshimen, forty or fifty miles north of Lengkou, and were repelled. This plainclothes team was originally composed of five elite soldiers selected from each company, who were determined to die if necessary, and were led by company and platoon leaders, distributed in key locations such as Huangtupo and Dashimenz, to maintain strict vigilance. On the 20th, the enemy used over a hundred cavalry to reconnoiter the front of our position. At 2 p.m. on the 21st, a combined force of over twenty armored vehicles, six or seven hundred infantry, and over a hundred cavalry launched a fierce attack on our plainclothes team. Platoon leader Ma fought bravely, hiding behind stone piles and earthen embankments, waiting for the enemy to approach before throwing grenades and shooting with pistols at distant targets, killing many enemies. In the end, due to the enemy's numerical superiority, the obstacles were destroyed by enemy tanks, and he was killed in action, with a dozen or so soldiers wounded and killed. The enemy then advanced to the vicinity of Huangtupo. (4) The Fierce Battle of Lengkou for Three Days and Nights: On March 22, after the enemy advanced to the vicinity of Yuanjia Yingzi, they began to attack our position fiercely. Our Division Commander Huang Guanghua personally led the Lin Regiment at the forefront, engaging in a fierce battle. From morning to night, the enemy gradually increased their infantry to about three thousand, with over ten artillery pieces, several tanks, and over a hundred armored vehicles. After a day of fierce fighting, they were repelled by our army. The enemy then increased their forces again and launched a large-scale attack, making the battle even fiercer. Our positions at Xiaojia Ying and Madaogou were repeatedly lost and regained, over a dozen times. Around 6 p.m., our army charged out of the position, destroying three enemy tanks and seven armored vehicles, and killing four or five hundred enemies. Division Commander Huang, with a righteous formation, fought the stubborn enemy for two days and nights. Despite the enemy's superior equipment, they were still fighting like trapped beasts. He then used unconventional tactics. That night, he added Jiang Regiment's Li Battalion, who, via Sidaogou, outflanked the enemy's right flank. At 4 a.m., they reached the front of the high ground southeast of Jiaolipu and launched a fierce attack on the enemy, driving them back around 10 a.m. and occupying the highlands around Gaolipu. At the same time, Guo Regiment's Dai Battalion was also dispatched (at the same time as Jiang Regiment's Li Battalion, they departed on separate routes) to outflank the enemy's left flank from Longwangmiao. However, due to the winding roads and enemy aircraft interference the next morning, the battalion advanced bravely and drove out the enemy from Yingtaoyuan at 4 p.m., occupying the area. These were all events of the 23rd. Our army's flanking attack on the enemy's rear had succeeded, and we immediately launched a frontal attack, engaging in fierce battles throughout the day. Both sides suffered heavy casualties. The battle on that day was as fierce as the battles of Gubei and Xifeng, and the enemy's aircraft were particularly active, forming teams of three or four aircraft and taking turns bombing our positions and the Lengkou and Jianchang areas. (6) The Enemy's Retreat: Previously, our General Commander, seeing that our army's continuous resistance had become increasingly fierce, went to the front line to supervise the battle on the 23rd. At that time, the Li and Dai Battalions were each bravely attacking the enemy. Li Battalion had occupied the northern highlands of Gaolipu, and Dai Battalion had also occupied the area around Shanshenmiao. As the fighting continued into the evening of the 24th, the enemy's momentum waned. Our army also suffered casualties, including five company commanders, over ten platoon leaders, and over three hundred soldiers. On the 25th, Zhang Kexun, the battalion commander of the Lin Regiment, personally led a courageous team of over two hundred men, launching a fierce night attack on the rear of the enemy's Jianjiayingzi, using grenades and broadswords to kill many enemies. The enemy wavered, and Battalion Commander Zhang died in action, deep in enemy territory. The enemy was therefore unable to expand their gains greatly. However, after this battle, the enemy suffered significant losses, and most of them withdrew to the rear of Xiaojiaying. The fighting also became more subdued. On that day, there was a strong wind and rain, and both sides reorganized. (6) Overview of Lengkou from the 26th of last month to the 4th of this month: After the 25th, our army continued to launch night attacks, as did the enemy. Both sides suffered heavy casualties. At 2 a.m. on the 29th, over a hundred enemies advanced to the vicinity of our Shanshenmiao, and were almost completely annihilated in our counterattack. After dawn, many weapons were collected, and many important documents were recovered from the enemy corpses. After this, the enemy infantry hid and did not come out, but over ten aircraft bombed our position every day. The bombing is still ongoing daily. Recently, it seems that they are concentrating their forces to attack our left flank. Our army is extremely vigilant and determined that there will be no other dangers. (7) General Commander Shang's Determination to Resist Japan: Our General Commander has been ordered to resist Japan and has a long-standing heart for serving the country, which you gentlemen know well. There is no need to say more about saving the country. Qilu also need not elaborate further. However, when we recovered Lengkou, I sent a telegram to Mr. Kong Yongzhi, in which I said, "If the enemy comes, I swear to die with them." Also, in the instructions to all officers and soldiers of our Corps, there are the words, "We will never allow anyone to take one inch or one foot of the land left by our ancestors." When he wrote these words, his tears fell with the writing, and his expression was passionate, moving all officers and soldiers. These two examples alone can show his determination to resist Japan. And the two phrases "With the enemy, there is no me; with me, there is no enemy" are the only creed in our Corps. (8) Hope for Spiritual Victory over Material: Our country's resistance to Japan this time is far inferior to the enemy in terms of material, which need not be explained in detail. Not only are our artillery and aircraft far behind, but even in terms of transportation, our army lacks heavy trucks. In terms of communication, our army lacks communication equipment. And even in terms of self-defense steel helmets, enemy-killing broadswords, and all the ordinary and necessary supplies for combat, almost none are available. In short, in terms of material, the enemy is superior everywhere, and we are inferior. However, the enemy has fast guns, but we have flesh and blood. The enemy has giant cannons, but we have courage. The enemy has aircraft circling in the air, but we have popular support filling the universe. In other words, the enemy has material, and we have spirit. The enemy can be defeated with a stick, and the will of the people is stronger than metal and stone. At this critical moment of life and death, if the soldiers do not risk their lives, it will not be enough to survive. If the masses are not of one mind, they cannot save the country. Therefore, we must hope for the unanimous assistance of the people of the country, so as to shield our rear."

Page 11

Sock Factory Runs Night Shifts, Disturbing People's Dreams, Lawsuit 145

Find ways to improve and reduce noise

Judge ordered exemption from punishment

There are many factories in the Public Concession, and residents are close together. However, the authorities have not yet divided the factory area or the residential area, so there are often factories adjacent to residents. If the factory has to do night work, the sound of the machines and the workers' shouts will inevitably be deafening all night long. Those who live nearby are disturbed by the noise and cannot sleep all night long, which has a great impact on the residents' peace. Recently, the Hua'an Sock Factory at No. 1027 Dexinli, Binlang Road, West Shanghai, has been running night shifts since last month, and the sound of the machines has been incessant all night long after 12 o'clock every night. The neighbors of the factory are all residents who deeply hate the noise of the factory, which makes them unable to sleep all night long. So their neighbors Li Yongde, Li Wenlou, Yan Xinpei, Xiao Zhang, and others went to the Gordon Road Police Station to report the situation of not being able to sleep and requested assistance. After the head of the police station went to the factory to investigate and found that it was true, Lawyer Ru Baoyi of the Legal Group of the Public Works Department represented the Bureau and filed a complaint with the First Special District Court against Cui Zhenghua, the owner of the Hua'an Factory, and Yu Dabao, the manager. However, China's Factory Law has not yet been promulgated, and there are no suitable clauses in the current law, so it is based on Article 36 of the Shanghai Municipal Council Yangjingbang Regulations, which states that the defendant released loud noises for no reason, disturbing the peace. The First Special Court has held a hearing once, and Shen Shanzeng, the magistrate, continued to summon the defendant yesterday morning. According to lawyer Ru, if the defendant's work does not harm others, the Public Works Department will not interfere. Now, the residents around the factory must serve for their occupations during the day, and they cannot rest at night. It is important to know that sleep is a right given to people by God and cannot be deprived by anyone. Although the defendant's noise was caused by work and not for no reason, the right of people to sleep has been infringed upon for no reason. In order to protect the peace of the residents, the Public Works Department filed a complaint and should be given relief. Li Yongde and others testified in court that they were disturbed by the loud noise of the factory at night, which made them unable to sleep. The defendant hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to defend, saying that the defendant was willing to improve the equipment in the factory, hoping to reduce the noise. Magistrate Shen then ordered the defendant to be exempted from punishment, ordering them to find ways to improve their equipment as soon as possible so that the noise would not disturb the peace of the neighbors, and to stop using the motor after 12 o'clock every night until dawn as much as possible. This unprecedented sleep case was concluded.

Further News on Dai Chengzhi Impersonating a Military Instructor 148

Dai Chengzhi from Wuxi, who impersonated a military instructor appointed by the Training Supervision Department and taught at Daxia University and Datong University, has been reported in this newspaper. It has now been found that the two schools each received an order from the Training Supervision Department through the post office one day before Dai Chengzhi came to the school, which roughly stated: "It has been found that high schools and above schools have implemented military training in accordance with the Ministry of Education's circular. Dai Chengzhi, a military instructor at the Wuxi Middle School, has been promoted to instructor at the university, etc." The two schools believed that the order from the Training Supervision Department was indeed sent from Nanjing, and the seals on the envelopes were authentic, so there was no doubt. The next day, Dai Chengzhi brought another letter of appointment from the Training Supervision Department to the school, met with the authorities, and discussed teaching hours and salary. A few days later, he started teaching on time. However, Daxia University believed that the school was not directly affiliated with the Training Supervision Department, and all official documents related to military training had always been forwarded by the Ministry of Education. It was doubtful why the department directly sent instructors to the school this time, so it reported the situation of the instructor coming to the school to the Ministry of Education. The Ministry of Education immediately consulted the Training Supervision Department and asked why the procedure for sending instructors to the school this time was wrong and requested a reply. Later, the Training Supervision Department replied that there was no promotion of Dai Chengzhi to instructor at the school and requested that the original order be returned to the school for investigation. At the same time, the Training Supervision Department telegraphed the local garrison headquarters to secretly arrest Dai. He was arrested at Daxia at 4 p.m. on the 10th of this month. It was found that Dai had received a total of 80 yuan in salary from Daxia in two installments. The report that he had borrowed 600 yuan from the school for marriage expenses was not true.

Li Chunshan's Family Appeals to the Municipal Government for Negotiations with Japan After His Abduction 151

It is heard that Li Chunshan has been sent back to Korea

Diao Degao is a henchman who deserves to be killed

It has been more than a month since Li Chunshan, the Korean revolutionary leader of Chinese nationality, was arrested on Luban Road. A few days ago, the Municipal Public Security Bureau arrested a Chinese traitor named Diao Degao, and it was learned that the case was indeed done by the Japanese. Recently, there has been a saying that Li Chunshan has been sent back to Korea by the Japanese police. Li's family yesterday submitted a petition to the Municipal Government, requesting it to negotiate with Japan according to law as soon as possible, and requesting that the traitor be executed. The original petition is as follows:

Petitioner Li Jinjingji, 45 years old, originally from Korea, registered in the Republic of China, currently residing at No. 54 Baokangli, Xiahfei Road, Shanghai, is appealing for a cross-border kidnapping and private repatriation, requesting a reasonable negotiation and strict punishment of the traitor in order to uphold the law and protect sovereignty. My husband, Li Chunshan, fled to Shanghai with his family in anger at the violent Japanese annexation of Korea. The Three Han patriots agreed to transport independence, and my husband also participated in it. Therefore, the Japanese hated my husband, no less than a thorn in their side, and often thought of getting him and being happy. Last year, after the Shanghai war ended, the bomb case in Hongkou Park arose. The chief culprit was greatly clumsy, and several people were killed and injured. The Japanese Consulate in Shanghai suspected that my husband was one of the masterminds and secretly ordered the Japanese police to search his residence in the French Concession. At that time, my husband happened to be out, so he was not caught, but the revolutionary comrade Mr. An Changhao was arrested. Because my husband could not live in peace in the Concession, he moved to the Chinese territory in Nanshi, relying on the protection of the local military police to ensure his safety. Unexpectedly, the Japanese police still sent plainclothes police to bribe traitors to investigate everywhere. On the evening of the ninth of last month, when my husband went to visit a friend on Luban Road, he was suddenly kidnapped by several Japanese police officers and put in a car and sped away. At that time, those who saw it on the road thought it was a bandit kidnapping and were afraid that there would be weapons and injuries, so they did not dare to stop him. Afterwards, the Second District Public Security Bureau sent detectives to investigate, but there was no news. Only that a traitor named Diao Degao had been arrested and was being interrogated. I could have quietly waited for the authorities to deal with it according to law, but suddenly saw in Chinese and foreign newspapers that my husband, Li Chunshan, had been sent back to Korea by the Japanese police and would be punished with severe penalties for subverting the government of the Japanese Empire. Upon hearing the news, I could not help but feel extremely sad. It was found that my family had already joined the Republic of China since the fall of the motherland and had a naturalization license No. 11 issued by the Ministry of Internal Affairs of the central government as proof. When my husband was kidnapped that day, it was on Luban Road in the Chinese territory. How could the Japanese ignore Chinese sovereignty and arrest him privately? Therefore, I am filing a detailed statement and asking you to negotiate reasonably as soon as possible to save my husband. At the same time, I earnestly request that the traitor Diao Degao, who colluded with the enemy to be a henchman, be executed to satisfy the hearts of the Chinese and Korean people, and my family will be grateful. Respectfully presented to Wu, the Mayor of Shanghai.

Tragic Death of a Young Woman in Yangjing Town, Pudong 158

Body Found in a Small Creek

Three Small Holes Found in the Top of Her Head

On the morning of the day before yesterday, at around 4 AM, a vegetable vendor passing by a small creek near the Bu Family Residence in the southern part of Yangjing Town, Pudong, discovered the body of a young woman floating on the surface. Nearby residents later identified her as the wife of Jiang A'gen, who lived in Jiang Family Lane to the west. The deceased's maternal family, upon learning of the incident, repeatedly gathered crowds to vandalize Jiang's house and belongings, causing a great disturbance. The detailed findings of the investigation are recorded below:

Discord Between Mother-in-Law and Daughter-in-Law 159

Jiang Si'hai, a local resident of No. 15 Jiang Family Lane in the southern part of Yangjing Town, is 43 years old. He has been working as a cook at the Huang family in Xiaonanmen, Shanghai. His wife, Gu, is 40 years old and has a son named A'gen, who is 23 years old and works in the cold work section of a steel factory. A'gen married a woman named Zhu in October of the year before last, but they have not had any children. The relationship between the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law may have been strained. Zhu moved to an old house at No. 21 to the west last summer. Because A'gen works away from home, he rarely returns. Zhu relied on selling vegetables to support herself, and the relationship between the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law was quite distant.

Body Floating in a Small Creek 160

Unexpectedly, Zhu suddenly went missing a few days ago. On the morning of the day before yesterday, at around 4 AM, her body was discovered floating in a small creek behind the residence of Tu Dong Bu Hezhou in the 25th Tu of Bu Family Residence. The nearby villagers were greatly shocked and came to watch. The body was then recovered, and it was observed that there were three small holes, about the size of mung beans, on the hairline of her head. The sight was very tragic. The Tu Dong reported the matter to the Third District Second Branch, requesting the local police to ask the local court to send personnel to investigate.

Only an Empty Shell Remains 161

After the case occurred, it caused a sensation in the surrounding area. After someone reported to the deceased's maternal family, believing that the mother-in-law, Gu, had always treated her daughter-in-law cruelly and suspected that she and her son had plotted to kill her, they immediately gathered dozens of strong men and rushed to the new house where Gu lived. First, they smashed all the dowry and clothing from the deceased's marriage, and then set them on fire. Then, they destroyed all the stoves, pots, tables, benches, and chopsticks in the three rooms of the eastern half of the new house, including the living room. Not satisfied, they gathered more people a second time to dismantle the doors, windows, and wall panels, leaving nothing intact. Yesterday morning, they gathered people for a third time to smash all the large and small utensils in the house, leaving nothing behind. Looking from the outside, only an empty shell of a house remained. Gu and her son had fled far away and dared not resist.

Results of the Investigation 162

After receiving the report, the local court immediately dispatched a prosecutor and his staff to the countryside to investigate. The investigation revealed that the small holes on the top of the deceased's head appeared to have been caused by iron nails. There were also several abrasions on her fingernails. Her body was bruised all over. However, it was difficult to determine whether these injuries were fatal wounds inflicted before her death or caused by someone after her death. It was also impossible to believe that she had committed suicide by drowning. After completing the investigation, the judge ordered that the mother-in-law, Gu, and the deceased's husband, A'gen, be arrested and brought to court for questioning. The body will be taken to the court for further examination.

Among the goods, those that are required to be filled in with a consignment note from the consulate-general, according to the statistics from the US Consulate-General, although there were increases and decreases compared to the same period last year, the total number was even smaller. Of the more important ones, among the edible animals, there were 5,447 pounds of frozen wild chickens, which were not exported in the same period last year; 10,157 pounds of sausages, while only 4,462 pounds in the same period last year; but frozen egg yolk decreased from 62,200 pounds to 29,340 pounds, and dried egg white also decreased from 6,800 pounds to 4,000 pounds. Animal hides and skins were exported to the United States in large quantities this year, such as 69,793 dan and 31,190 pounds of sheep and lambskins, while in the same period last year, it was 106,248 dan and 26,513 pounds; 2,234,358 dan and 2,996,831 pounds of goat and lambskins, while in the same period last year, it was 1,354,470 dan and 1,820,979 pounds; deer skins were not exported; rabbit skins were 29,993 pounds, weasel skins were 595,063 pounds, and 452,221 pounds in the same period last year; pig bristles decreased from 127,720 pounds to 47,292 pounds; feathers decreased from 270,724 to 161,605 pounds; tea increased several times compared to the same period last year, with a ratio of 664,121 to 342,967 pounds; sesame was shipped to the US at 5,179,839 pounds, while it was not exported in the same period last year; galls were exported at 46,725 pounds, and they were not exported in the same period last year. Among the textiles, cotton waste increased from 10,634 to 24,000 pounds, miscellaneous cotton fabrics decreased from 26,049 pounds to 24,245 pounds, woolen blankets were exported at 1,518,075 pounds, while they were not exported in the same period last year; raw silk and silk waste also increased significantly compared to the same period last year, with raw silk increasing from 38,899 pounds to 61,317 pounds, silk waste being exported at 98,121 pounds, while it was not exported in the same period last year; silk fabrics were exactly the opposite, with a ratio of 4,718 to 43,880 pounds; straw hats increased from 864,980 to 948,061, and straw products decreased from 258,470 to 58,644 pounds.

Xin Chang He Steamer is Now Out of Danger 164

Expected to Arrive in Yichang This Morning

Further Repairs Required in Shanghai

The Xin Chang He steamer, owned by Jardine Matheson and operating on the Yichang-Chongqing route, ran aground on the Konglin Shoal on the 3rd of this month. This has already been reported previously. According to a telegram received yesterday by Jardine Matheson from its Yichang branch, the passengers and cargo on board the Xin Chang He had been transferred to the Mei Lu. The ship was then refloated. After patching up the hole, it was towed by the Mei Lu yesterday and is expected to arrive in Yichang this morning. After some minor repairs in Yichang, it will come to Shanghai for dock inspection and repairs.

Reduction of Shallow Water Fees on the Hankou-Yichang Route 165

A Reduction of 25% First on the 15th

All to be Cancelled Next Month

During the winter shallow water period on the Hankou-Yichang route, various companies increased the shallow water fee by 50% starting from January 17th of this year. This has been in effect for several months. Recently, the water level on the route has gradually risen, and ships directly from Shanghai to Yichang have resumed their schedules. According to a notice received by the various shipping companies in Shanghai from the Hankou branch yesterday, regarding the shallow water fee on the Hankou-Yichang route, it was decided by the five companies to first reduce it by 25% starting on the 15th of this month, leaving a remaining 25%, which will be completely cancelled from May 1st. The companies have already informed the various customs brokers.
