Of course, this is only the beginning and cannot be fully considered a realization, but if everyone can work hard and start from themselves, the bright future of building several national products families is what we earnestly hope for.

Wuxi Women and National Products 222

— Shousong

At a time when the national crisis is serious and the voice of the national products movement is noisy for a while, the national products movement in Wuxi is of course also very prosperous. According to the reporter's observation, Wuxi women's understanding of national products has the following two different trends:

Production: Women belonging to this category account for the majority. They spend their days buried in factories and homes, accelerating their production. Women in factories mostly use their hands and feet to operate machines. What they earn every day can maintain their lives and have something left over; those in families mostly do their handmade lace industry, and their income is also quite considerable; although the above are all engaged in the production of national products, they are actually driven by life. They don't have a deep understanding and recognition of national products themselves; as for what they use, it is indeed authentic national products.

Consumption: Those belonging to this category are a small number of "leisured class." What they use, even they themselves cannot accurately recognize whether it is national products or foreign goods. In short, they only seek "fashionable," "eye-catching," "touching," "......" As for what is national products? Why should national products be used? They have no time to care!

In addition, in the business world, there are women's national products stores, etc., but the efficiency is still very low. If you want to promote it widely, I am afraid there is still a need for large-scale publicity!

How Smart Housewives Choose Clothing Materials 223

— Ye Shaoming

Of the four basic necessities of life, clothing is the first item. Clothing is a tool to protect the body and for the sake of hygiene, one must pay attention to it, which everyone knows, but what we want to study, especially women's clothing, is what kind of material is the most economical, most beautiful, and most hygienic?

Generally, people who advocate frugality say that only cloth is the best, the price is cheap, the style is simple, and it can be washed frequently to maintain cleanliness and hygiene.

However, we have had an experience that tells us that using silk to make clothes is actually more economical and worthwhile than cloth. In our grandfather's era, when we opened the box, we often saw many silk clothes that his father or his grandfather had passed on to him, and our grandfather, inheriting this inheritance, could not only enjoy wearing it himself, but also resize it and make small clothes for his sons and grandsons to wear. This is a fact. When I was eight or nine years old, I did wear the silk clothes left by my grandfather, remade and worn to relatives' houses during the New Year to wish them well.

At least we can understand that silk clothes are indeed more durable than cloth clothes. Because silk is made of silk, it is naturally stronger than cotton yarn and has a longer lifespan. Cloth clothes are easily soiled, so they must be washed frequently, and frequent washing makes them easy to break; and because they are cloth clothes, they are not very cherished when worn, and are particularly easy to stain. Only when wearing silk clothes, one must pay special attention to avoid staining them. Moreover, silk fabrics are less likely to be stained than cloth, so of course there is no need to wash them, or no need to wash them often. Not washing them or not washing them often makes them less likely to break. According to an experienced housewife, the lifespan of a silk garment is roughly equivalent to three or four cloth garments; foreign silk or rayon fabrics are, of course, exceptions.

The beauty and cleanliness of clothing are very important to people's interest or sympathy, especially for women. If they are disheveled, they lose beauty and reduce pleasure, so I think it is best to make women's clothes with silk; as for whether the price is extravagant and whether it is suitable for hygiene, it is also very clear.

Since a silk garment can be equivalent to the lifespan of three or four cloth garments, then we assume that making four cloth garments costs four yuan and five cents for the fabric and four yuan for the labor, then it costs eight yuan and five cents; while the silk price only costs four yuan for the fabric and two yuan for the labor because it is only one garment, totaling only six yuan and five cents. Isn't wearing silk clothes cheaper than cloth clothes?

As for hygiene, silk fabrics are less likely to be stimulated to the skin by sudden changes in climate than cotton fabrics, which everyone has experienced, so silk clothes are also better than cloth clothes.

Recently, foreign goods have been flooding the market. People below the middle class buy foreign cloth or rayon woven fabrics to make clothes, while people above the middle class buy silk fabrics, which have always been very expensive and extremely insecure, with huge annual losses.

This year is the year of national products, and everyone is advocating national products. Many people think that if you want to buy national clothing materials, you can only buy domestic cloth. However, women who love beauty are also complaining that there are too few types of domestic cloth, and the patterns and dyeing are also less than foreign cloth, so they are forced to promote national products and have to buy some domestic cloth to make clothes, but they still go to department stores to cut imported silk.

In fact, they have not noticed that domestic silk factories have also developed very well in recent years. There are many types, and the patterns and dyeing are also emerging endlessly, which are no different from imported goods, and the price is 50% to 70% cheaper than imported goods. We only need to walk into various national products companies or silk stores to visit, such as Meya Silk Weaving Factory's Jiu Man silk, Ningxiang brocade, brocade crepe, plaid double crepe, Liu Tiao double crepe, and georgette, all of which are very good and cheap, and are completely beautiful clothing materials for modern women.

We should not be superstitious about foreign goods, let them increase other people's ambition; nor should we buy inferior clothing materials without thinking. We should carefully consider what is domestic, economical, beautiful, and hygienic before buying.

Experienced housewives probably all know: "Clothing does not differ by an inch, shoes do not differ by a point." If there is a slight uneconomical act, it will be consumed invisibly, and the annual accumulation of a family will be incalculable.

Women do not have to hide the need for decoration, as long as the decoration is within the economic conditions, what is not to be happy about? If you spend money for decoration and promote sales of foreign goods, that is what smart and patriotic women disdain to do.

As for children's clothing and husbands' clothing, they are probably also controlled by the housewife. We also hope that the housewife will think carefully about whether to buy domestic silk for her husband or use her own or her husband's old silk clothes to remake them for the children, which should be considered by the smart housewife. Sometimes, it is very common for a silk garment to be worn old, dyed once or twice, and remade for wearing again; and it is still very neat and beautiful when worn.

— Ke Ding'an

This may be a good phenomenon! At the beginning of the first and second quarters of the Year of National Products, it is a very fortunate thing to have such achievements and contributions to national products.

What We Expect from Housewives 225

— Zhou Chenghun

"Modern housewives must recognize their goals. They are in an important position. It is not enough to be a virtuous wife and good mother who obeys the three obediences and four virtues and educates their children. They should step into society, integrate with society, and jointly bear the burden of saving the country with national products!" Before writing this article, I must first faithfully dedicate this passage to the general housewives.

Because the majority of society is a collection of many families, and the family is a major outlet for material consumption, while housewives are the masters who manage the family.

Judging from the situation in the past, it can be arbitrarily said that housewives did not have a full understanding of national products. For daily necessities, food, clothing, and enjoyment, as long as the style is satisfactory and the price is reasonable, they are no longer happy to care about whether they are national products or not. The husband happily bought imported goods back, or added one or two foreign toys for the children, and they had no intention of examining whether they were national products! As a result, in Jinli Lane and the Three Companies, there was a lot of traffic, and they worked hard to be volunteer salesmen for foreign goods, which is really heartbreaking to say. As a result, promotion is just promotion, and foreign goods still have loyal users. This contradictory and alarming phenomenon continues to this day.

Fortunately, the recent trend of national products is gradually approaching women. Some women are very unwilling to lag behind and are paying attention to national products. However, it is not effective to rely solely on high-profile theories and unrealistic promotion. Housewives should first examine their responsibilities in their own positions. That is to say: all utensils and utensils for food, clothing, housing, and transportation in the family, as well as items consumed in social activities and exchanges, should first make a determination "only national products are allowed," and even half a thread, a shoe, or a small towel should have the ambition to "swear to use national products." Secondly, supervising the husband's purchase of items and indoctrinating the children with the spirit of using national products are also the urgent tasks of housewives!

However, women do not have a group that can study and consider the whole. It is always felt that it is too unsystematic to implement it on their own. It is best to form several associations to study and train women's understanding and use of national products in a comprehensive and thorough manner. At the same time, please invite several national products experts to guide them in using various methods to promote to the lower-level women's circles so that all women can raise their heads and pay attention to national products.

Recently, aren't the men and women in the society have an organization called "Family Renewal Association"? This is a good opportunity to strive to instill the love of national products into women. I often think that the preliminary problem of family renewal and family improvement at present is still the use of national products. I hope that many housewives can earnestly follow the society to jointly bear this important mission.

Introducing an Inventor of National Products Condensed Milk 226

— Wang Yuehui

Condensed milk is something that our country has never manufactured. However, it has been sold very well in recent years. According to customs statistics, the annual import amount reaches 20 million yuan. The Chinese people did not try to recover this huge loss. If this continues, how can we imagine it? There is Mr. Xiao Jia Gan who, after feeling painful, determined to make condensed milk himself to replace it. After experiencing setbacks, he finally succeeded. So far, the Yan brand condensed milk cocoa milk, etc., sold on the market are all domestic goods. Now, I will briefly introduce the process of Mr. Xiao's establishment of the condensed milk company for the purpose of commendation.

Mr. Xiao Jia Gan is a native of Jiaxing, Zhejiang Province. After graduating from the Department of Business Administration of Fudan University in the 13th year of the Republic of China, he served in the Qingdao Shandong Provincial Bank. One day, Mr. Xiao happened to talk with friends about the prosperity of imported condensed milk in China and was deeply angry. He then intended to manufacture condensed milk in order to recover the rights and interests in case of one. However, he thought that he was not a milk production expert. If he engaged in it hastily, it would be difficult to succeed. So he began to investigate. He purchased and read a large number of Western books on milk business, milk product manufacturing methods, etc., and strove to learn for the preparation of practical management.

Mr. Xiao's special ambition was determined, so he resolutely resigned from his job in the bank and went south to return to Zhejiang. On the one hand, he taught at the Zhejiang Provincial Commercial Middle School to maintain his livelihood. On the other hand, he joined forces with friends Tu Bushan and Qiu Shilin to establish a sterilized milk company to seek experience. In his spare time, he tested condensed milk production. After 127 trials, he repeatedly failed and then continued to succeed. However, condensed milk machines such as vacuum machines and crystallizers were worth more than 100,000 yuan and had to be ordered from abroad. Mr. Xiao's family was poor. Such a large sum of money was difficult to raise. His ambition was frustrated. One day, he happened to see a slogan hanging on the roadside saying, "Where there is a will, there is a way." He could not help but be deeply moved and determined to be more determined. Then he went to a certain Japanese bookstore and repeatedly obtained the machine books catalog, intending to copy it according to the map. Friends all laughed at him for being crazy and did not believe him. However, Mr. Xiao still encouraged himself to proceed. He often drew machine sketches at the desk at midnight. Although he was often sick, he did not care. In the winter of the 18th year of the Republic of China, Mr. Xiao followed the drawn sketch and followed its description procedure to implement the imitation of the three sets of vacuum machine sterilizer crystallizer. At first, the material matching was very inappropriate. After many disassemblies, all the machines were finally successful in the winter of the 19th year. So he collected 60,000 yuan of capital and established the West Lake Condensed Milk Company. He purchased cows, built sheds, and added machines. In the winter of the 20th year, he sold Yan brand condensed milk and cocoa milk on the market. At present, overseas Chinese in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Nanyang have come to purchase. It is really cheap (condensed milk is sold for 20 yuan per box, cocoa milk is sold for 30 yuan per box) and the quality is good. Compared with imported goods, there is nothing that is not as good as it is.

At present, the company has more than 1,000 acres of pasture and more than 2,700 dairy cows. The scale is gradually expanding. Xiao is aware that the capital is small and insufficient for development. So he came to Beijing a month ago to state the founding process to the central government and asked for assistance. He was deeply praised by the central committee members Chen Lifu and Yu Jingtang, who promised to find ways to solicit shares. This small amount should not be difficult to raise in the shortest possible time. The company's future is immeasurable.

Worth Introducing Chongqing National Goods Introduction Center (Part 2) 227

According to the value of goods imported into Sichuan Province in the past three years, the annual value is approximately 30 million taels, of which foreign goods account for about 80%. The outflow of economic rights is considerable. In addition, the farmers in our province follow old habits, which are not perfect. Not only is the cost of imported goods higher, but also the collapse and escape of farmers in Shanghai have led to the gradual disappearance of the Sichuanese community's credit in Shanghai. The process of the Sichuanese community generally purchasing goods in other ports is as follows:

Each level charges fees, and each level divides profits. We should find ways to eliminate these practices to reduce the cost of goods. We have been planning this for a long time. This year, Mr. Zhang Yujiu of the Bank of China came to Sichuan, and we discussed the lack of vitality in the national goods sales market and sought ways to improve it. We deeply agreed on this issue, and then initiated the organization of the China National Goods Introduction Center. In June of this year, the initiators publicly elected Mr. Tong Shaosheng and Mr. Chen Shujing to go to Shanghai to investigate and negotiate. We were warmly supported by Mr. Zhang Gongquan and guided by important figures from the Bank of China to visit more than 40 national goods factories. We negotiated with each factory to establish sales methods. Because we urgently needed to prepare internally, we only stayed for more than 40 days before returning to Chongqing. The center was officially established on October 1st and began its introduction work. Based on the center's organizational motive, we plan to simplify the aforementioned goods purchasing process as follows:

From the diagram above, our center is essentially the factory's exclusive agent and the direct representative of the Shanghai China National Goods Production and Sales Association. This reduces some unnecessary waste. With the support of the Bank of China, our center can purchase goods on behalf of customers, reducing costs and simplifying procedures. At the same time, the Sichuanese community's credit in the financial circles of other ports may be slightly restored with the establishment of a statutory and organized group. In short, the organization of the introduction center is essentially a public buying agent for the Sichuanese community to purchase goods in other places. It aims to make the greatest possible contribution to local firms or wholesalers, without any intention or tendency to encroach on their interests. The center's economic objective is based on saving various fees to promote the sales of national goods, and there is no conflict with the interests of various firms or wholesalers.

The features of our center are summarized as follows:

(A) For Manufacturers

(1) Limited company registration with legal protection

(2) Manufacturers' trading partners can be simplified

(3) Cost-effective and useful advertising services

(4) Market research can be requested by letter to the center

(5) Suggestions for improvement are always welcome

(6) Direct sales by the factory, striving to expand the target

(B) For Merchants

(1) The latest product samples can be selected locally

(2) Only a 30% deposit is required for the factory to ship goods

(3) Payment and pickup upon reaching the order

(4) Exchange rates can be settled at any time within 30 days

(5) Flexible financing can be arranged if funds are occasionally lacking

(6) Sincere service regardless of quantity

However, this is a pioneering effort, and we lack experience. We hope that patriotic and enlightened people will not hesitate to offer advice to correct our shortcomings. We would be grateful! The future of national goods would be fortunate!

A Glimpse of the Children's Amusement Market Held by the China National Goods Company (Part 2) 228

— Ke Ding'an

Turning into "National Goods Avenue" from "Ooh-Ooh Road," a long line of "cars," "carriages," "airplanes," "bicycles," etc., are arranged in the center of the avenue. On both sides are signs for "parking." Next to "National Goods Avenue" is "Innocence Road," displaying "children's clothing": Zhongshan suits, school uniforms, world suits, knitted and cotton suits, as well as shirts, undershirts, bibs, diapers, etc., all displayed in a very interesting way. In the "Socks Department," they piled many socks into the three characters "Children's Day." There are also "cosmetics," "pharmaceuticals," etc., all displayed there.

The new-style equipment on "Jump-Jump Road," such as "tanks," "machine guns," "rifles," etc., will make children feel that they must have a martial spirit to contribute to the country! "Little Girls" are making various pleasing poses. Celluloid lions, tigers, dogs, horses, etc., also have a "can't be subdued by power" look.

"Run-Run Road" is a "children's food world," displaying many kinds of candies and biscuits. There are weapon-style candies, which are very novel. When Yang'er saw many tank-style candies, he liked them very much. He said, "I want to use them to fight our enemies in the future." I bought two for him and said to him, "But don't forget after you finish eating the candies!"

The horses, carriages, bicycles, horse-drawn carts on "Lively Road," as well as small "steel essence," "electric powder," "porcelain," "electric appliances," etc., are very suitable for children's psychology.

There are many slogans posted in the market. Now I will introduce several to children who have not participated in the inland:

Unfortunately, due to space limitations, we were unable to accommodate all of them, and some valuable works may have been missed. We apologize for this. We will consider publishing them in future issues to fulfill your intentions. In the future, please stamp your submissions to facilitate verification when claiming payment, otherwise, payment will be declined.

Spring and Autumn

Abolishing Taels and Changing to Dollars: A Hundred Combinations 230

—

"Abolishing taels and changing to dollars" is a bloodless revolution that should be specially recorded in the history of Chinese finance.

An "old-timer" in the "silver money industry" said that exchanging silver for silver dollars, then converting silver dollars back into taels, and then converting taels back into silver dollars, with "two adding one and making five, three adding one and making thirty-one," requires continuous calculations on the thirteen-bead abacus, as long as there is an entry, no matter how troublesome. It can turn one tael of silver into no money at all, just like a Shandong villager performing magic.

The co-existence of "taels" and "dollars," is it harming the people or harming business? We still need "national experts" to express their opinions, but the "tael" is causing trouble in the financial world, and there is ironclad evidence of this.

In fact, the "tael" does many evil things. For example, European and American countries are very affectionate to our country on the one hand, and secretly flirt with Japan on the other hand. This is "two-faced." Northern China is fighting with Japanese soldiers, fists and feet, cannons and knives, while in the South, they still shake hands with the Japanese, promoting diplomacy and friendship. This is riding a "two-headed horse." Let's talk about family problems. One son inherits two lines, marrying two wives, called "two big heads." But "three days early at the temple gate makes you big," even mud bodhisattvas must follow two rules and follow one order, newcomer slow down, no courtesy, at most give a title "vice wife." If not, the family will be in trouble, and the kitchen god will move house, and from then on, the family will have many problems.

The Ming Dynasty Kangxi Dictionary says that "tael" means "two," and "dollar" means "one." "The great road loses sheep because of many forks." The great road of life, having one is enough. We Chinese are wandering everywhere, just suffering from not being willing to "stay with one to the end" and "go all the way to the end." "There are no two suns in the sky, and no two kings for the people." You want to be a hero, I want to be a good man, this road is not open. Now, "abolishing taels and changing to dollars," everyone starts from scratch, and perhaps China can be saved. Someone said, "Abolishing taels and changing to dollars, one becomes two, and two becomes one!" Alas, "this is really A Yuan wearing a hat, it's over!"

Two Kinds of Wrongfully Dead and Drunken Fools Live 231

—

In Shanghai, every year during the "spring" and "winter" seasons, there are often many people who "die unjustly." These "wrongfully dead" people die in two different ways, but both are sacrificed due to carelessness in their diet and daily life.

In the spring months of February and March, newspapers often report news of "death from eating pufferfish roe poisoning." Most of the victims are laborers from Jiangbei. They pick up pufferfish roe in garbage cans, or buy pufferfish roe cheaply, and after cooking and eating it at home, they develop poisoning, with abdominal distension and pain, writhing and screaming, and mostly die after ineffective treatment; some even die as a whole family. Good people sacrifice their precious lives for the sake of satisfying their appetites. This kind of death can be considered "wrongful death."

In winter, when the weather is cold, newspapers often report news of "death from coal briquette poisoning." They are also economical families, living in small rooms, and when it's cold, they burn coal briquettes for warmth and close the windows tightly. Because the air is not circulating, they are poisoned by coal gas. People gradually faint, and some die as a whole family from poisoning. Readers can only sigh after reading the newspaper: "Poor 'wrongful death'?"

The above two kinds of "wrongful deaths" continue to occur during these two seasons, like clockwork articles. The reason for this is that they lack common sense and are unaware of the danger. We also have to blame social education for not being popularized, which leads to such ignorant people and such tragic results.

According to medical records: pufferfish are highly toxic. Decoction of reed root and olives can be taken to detoxify. The roe is even more toxic. Soaking it in water overnight will make it as large as gorgon fruit. Those who are poisoned can be effectively treated by quickly stir-frying Sophora japonica flowers and grinding them with dried rouge in equal parts, mixing with water and administering orally. Because poisoning from eating pufferfish roe is often fatal, it is specially noted here for reference. Both items are available in pharmacies.

Gengdi on Fire and Snow Ming

At noon, the sunlight thinly spills on the cultivated embankment, applying a layer of hazy color. The fine grasses of the winter stretch their lazy waists, breathing in the exotic fragrance of the fields. The wind blows faintly, and the grass dances its green shirt, startling the white butterfly clinging to it, which flies away.

Along both sides of the river are all ridges, overshadowed by willow trees planted every five steps, so the grass is not easily scorched. The willow leaves are long, and the color has changed from tender yellow to emerald green, clinging to the swaying branches, some lowering their heads to look at their own postures in the water, and some straightening their bodies, staring at the distant spring sky, but all reflect their shadows on the calm warm waves.

In order to breathe in the air of the spring fields, I dragged my rattan cane and strolled to the riverside. After passing the stone bridge, I came directly to the cultivated embankment. Standing on the embankment, I leisurely pondered in the vast expanse of nature, the warm breeze was blowing, the sunlight was bathing, and the subtle sounds of nature were playing, so I could forget the difficulties of the past and covet the interest of being out of the world. So I stopped.

In the silence, the sound of water suddenly rang out, as if paddles were hitting the water surface, and a faint whistle came from afar. Looking back, a fishing boat floated down on the narrow, other end of the azure stream. The slender boat, like a piece of seaweed, gradually approached. It could be seen that the sides of the boat were full of black, long-beaked birds, which we call "touching fish public" in our hometown, which are actually the cormorants mentioned in the Erya. Du Gongbu's poem "Jiangzhong Xunhe He Feiyan," the Xunhe is this kind of waterfowl that is best at catching fish underwater.

The fisherman, holding a long bamboo pole and blowing a whistle, drove the cormorants into the water. They plunged their duck-like necks into the water, and after a long time, they came up, accurately spitting out two or three fish from their mouths. Because their necks were tied with ropes, even though there were fish in their mouths, they still could not swallow them to satisfy their hunger. This seems to be a Lesson also for those who make wedding clothes for others.

As usual, the fisherman grabs the cormorant's neck, hangs it upside down, and the cormorant raises its head, and then instinctively hangs down, spitting out carp or white small fish from its plough-like beak. The fisherman catches it easily and puts it in the basket, and then laughs. The cormorant itself doesn't understand for whom it is living.

No matter how far the fishing boat sails, the cormorant will follow the fishing boat underwater, just like a released white pigeon will fly back thousands of miles; the value of each cormorant is thirty yuan at most.

Gradually, the fishing boat passed through the river bay, and the black-feathered waterfowl was still diligently working. The fisherman leisurely supported his bamboo pole and whistled, shielded by the green shade of the willow, and then could no longer be seen.

Although I have no feelings and no sorrow, if I am not a cormorant, why am I also looking for fish for others day and night!

Viewing Precious Records 232

— Fei Wenbao

Mr. Zhang Wendi and his classmate Mr. Ma Tingdong obtained a large jadeite stone five or six years ago. They carved it into a pagoda, two palace lanterns, and an archway. I took the time to view them a few days ago. The pagoda is divided into seven stories, more than three feet high, with electric lights inside, radiating precious light and full of emerald green color. The two palace lanterns are carved with landscapes on the outside. The green parts are carved into mountains and forests, full of verdant green, extremely beautiful. According to Mr. Ma, it took several years of effort and hundreds of man-hours to complete this crystallization. The executors are slightly negligent, and all previous efforts will be wasted. I heard that you will be taking them to the American exhibition for display soon. I said that this is enough to promote the magic of our country's carving and the greatness of art, not just to show off precious treasures for a while. On that day, many Westerners were among the appreciators. Dr. Mei Lanfang and scholar Zhu Fuxiu also came to a stop. (Payment declined)

Petals 233

— Jin Guangzhen

Those who only know how to eat but don't know how to work are parasites in society, the most shameful and disgusting villains of mankind.

In a person's life, nothing happens a second time. The beggar Yuan Qi continued to smile after death; perhaps he was thanking God for eliminating the root of his pain?

Time flows like a river, never to return; life is also like this丨丨丨easy to grow old.

Warm bedding is the enemy of youth.

The life of the rich is tedious; the life of the poor is happy.

Long Novel

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 234

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 4: The 情局 Resumes at the Teahouse, Accumulating Affection; the Year-End is Difficult to Pass, the Pawnshop Makes a Mournful Sound

Walking to the door of the milk tea shop, Ji Zhi rushed forward and said: It's here. Pointing at the door of the shop. Gui Zhi twisted her body and said: Second Master, please go, I'm not going. Ji Zhi said: Now that we've come to this door, why not go in and sit for five minutes? Please, please, please. Saying that, he used all his strength, only to be polite. At this time, Gui Zhi couldn't help but hum slightly in her nose, seeming to sigh, so she had to follow him in a reluctant manner. In this milk tea shop, three tables were placed outside the counter. Ji Zhi looked at it. Although there were no customers at this time, he didn't want to sit in such an open place, so he looked around. He hadn't said anything yet, but a waiter sitting by the stove warming himself had already come forward and said with a smile: There are elegant seats inside, there are two elegant seats inside. He had already led the way, lifted a white cloth curtain, let them into an outer room, and put down the door curtain by the way. Ji Zhi thought to himself that even though Haidian was a town, it had opened this kind of business similar to a café in the city, and there were indeed waiters who understood business to entertain them. After Gui Zhi entered the room, she didn't sit down, but only raised her head to look at a framed landscape painting hanging on the wall. The waiter brought in two hot towels, and asked with a smile: What would you two like to eat? Ji Zhi then asked Gui Zhi what she would like to eat. Gui Zhi took the towel in her hand, rubbing her hands together, but she still looked at the landscape painting. She casually replied: I'm easy. Ji Zhi thought that she wouldn't drink coffee, and ordered an lotus root powder for her: he ordered a cocoa for himself. He also greeted her to sit down, please sit down. Gui Zhi took off the scarf on her body, sat opposite Ji Zhi, and kept folding the scarf on the table. She lowered her head, didn't speak, and didn't look at Ji Zhi. When the waiter brought the food, there were originally plates of dry snacks on the table, so he didn't have to come in. Ji Zhi took two sips of cocoa, and then put two pieces of cake and peach cake from the plate in front of her, and then said: Please use a little. Don't misunderstand me and be angry with me. I'm eating my brother's food now, don't think I'm a second master, I don't dare to offend any of the servants and old maids in the family. Because of this, even if they offended you, I can't do anything. (40)

Traveling in Art

Mei Lanfang's Recent Conversation 235

— Wheel

Mr. Mei Lanfang is currently living in Shanghai, and occasionally travels to Jiangsu, Zhejiang and other places. Yesterday, when the reporter met him, he inquired about the number of grains, and the answers are recorded as follows:

(Question) I saw in the newspaper the other day that Mr. Zu Bu had a conversation with Mr. Song Chunfang, in which he discussed the idea of adding Western music to Chinese dramas, and mentioned Mr. Li Shizeng's words about the bodhisattva sitting on an airplane, is this true?

(Answer) I am very familiar with Mr. Chunfang. I did have a conversation with him about drama the other day. The real content was: Mr. Song advocated that the music of Chinese dramas should be improved. Since he is not an expert in music himself, he asked for my opinion. I replied that I also think it needs to be improved, because I think that the music of Chinese dramas is indeed too simple. I have long held this view and have had various trials. For example, since I came on stage, I have restored the four-stringed moon lute; added the Suhu to set off the Huqin; added the Jiu Yin; added the碰镜; and applied the drum to dance. All of these were promoted by me, and have become fashionable on the stage for fifteen or sixteen years. But I still think that the music of Peking opera is still insufficient, so when I was in Beiping, I created two kinds of Huqin, one high-pitched; one mid-pitched; and one low-pitched. Unfortunately, the results of the trial were not satisfactory, so I once intended to add Western music to Chinese dramas. But my intention is only to participate in the creation of Cantonese opera stages, which is admirable, but it seems that more cooperation and improvement are needed. As for talking with Mr. Song, I did not mention Mr. Shizeng and the bodhisattva sitting on an airplane, because I only saw this in the newspaper this time, and I couldn't even talk about making any explanations (Question) I heard that you intend to not play the role of Dan or change to playing the role of Xiaosheng in spoken dramas due to your age, is this true?

(Answer) I think it's okay to sing a few more years according to the precedent in the drama world, but I have to perform the appropriate dramas. Now I haven't considered this issue in detail. As for changing to playing the role of Xiaosheng in spoken dramas, I am very willing to study it, but there is no possibility of trying it without pure research.

(Question) The newspaper reported that you have the intention of playing Madame Butterfly with Ms. Hu Die, as well as various sound films, is this true?

(Answer) I only know about the Madame Butterfly thing from the newspaper. I have only met the stars in the film industry at the banquets of various film companies. As for sound films and any film dramas, I am considering them, and I have not made any decisions with any companies. The so-called 100,000 yuan performance of Farewell My Concubine is also an April Fool's Day style news. Finally, Mr. Mei told us that the reason why he stayed in Shanghai was because he was a native of Suzhou, so he planned to visit the spring scenery of Jiangnan in time. He also plans to visit the ports of the Yangtze River in the near future, and it is not certain whether he will go to Mount Lu.

The Abnormal Phenomenon of Women's Occupations 236

— Silver Thread

Women's occupations in today's society have long been in the same position as men. But in practical observations, it is still a kind of deformed development recently. A certain organization published an advertisement to recruit female employees, and as a result, Ms. A and Ms. B, two women with graceful figures and charming appearances, were selected after a strict selection process. They have been working with peace of mind since then, and they are very happy. But sitting there all day long, except for a few colleagues who often joke and tease them, they are simply holding positions without doing anything. After more than a month like this, Ms. B had already become intimate with them, getting along like fish and water. Ms. A, on the other hand, was the exact opposite, always maintaining her icy and stern attitude, never showing the slightest smile. And being in such a boring environment, she was even more secretly surprised and did not know what was going on. A few days later, Ms. B suddenly came to visit, and said a word of special representation of male colleagues to clearly express and persuade her to change her mind, otherwise, please leave early and make other plans. Ms. A then woke up as if from a dream and suddenly understood. It turned out that the two of them were hired by a joint venture of several colleagues, not employed by the organization. It is said that the purpose of their employment is to adjust the boring atmosphere in the office!

This novel anecdote is indeed a side shadow of women's occupations in a deformed society. We really feel very sigh. At the same time, I watched a movie similar to this, "Women's Cry" by Mingxing Company. It made me even more emotional. This film gives a realistic description of the corner of women's occupations. The description is painful and powerful, and moving. It is a good work needed by the times. Originally, "Cries" are the tragic cries of the oppressed. I don't know what the female compatriots will think after reading it?

Free Talk

Saving the Nation Through Leisure 237

— Da Wu

"During times of national crisis," one can discern the busyness of important figures from the newspapers. Thus, while it's not necessary for every important person to have their own airplane, anyone with their own airplane is undoubtedly an important person. Soaring through the clouds, flying high and low, today "inspecting" somewhere, tomorrow "overseeing" somewhere else, in Beijing in the morning, yet in Shanghai in the afternoon – how swift and convenient! The so-called "entire plan" and "determination to resist Japan" are all conceived on these airplanes. And once they realize the difficulty and retreat, they can transfer the plane to another important person as a farewell gift, a sign of continued reliance, "another task for you," to mark their unforgettable service. The use of airplanes is truly significant.

However, from the newspapers, one can also see the leisurely and self-satisfied demeanor of these important figures, poised and at ease. For example, in the newspapers a few days ago, there was a news item with a floral border about "Chairman □'s Leisurely Interests." According to my experience reading newspapers, news items with floral borders are particularly valuable. This headline is tantamount to saying: even the Chairman has become so leisurely, naturally the world is at peace, the national crisis has passed, and the people can well "play mahjong." The gist of the news was that "Chairman □ today visited an old bookstore in plain clothes to purchase several ancient books and antiques," and walked back to his office. (Note from Da: Because it was a special dispatch, this sentence was not in the telegram, probably to save on telegraph fees, so it was not detailed.) As the Chairman, buying a few ancient books and antiques is naturally a minor matter, and since national etiquette does not prohibit playing golf or dancing the Charleston, it certainly does not prohibit buying old books and antiques. Moreover, removing official attire and going out in plain clothes is much more respectable and endearing than traveling in a high carriage with four horses, with attendants shouting and clearing the way.

However, the phrase "plain clothes" somehow reminds me of the officials in old novels who were known for their integrity and fairness, "traveling incognito for private visits," and the young masters and sons who committed great disasters and "fled in disguise." Fortunately, Chairman □'s "plain clothes" trip was to buy books at an old book stall, and there was no danger. In earlier times, private visits and escapes were always worrying. However, this also shows the composure and calmness of the important figures, at ease and self-possessed. On the same day's newspaper, there was also a piece about General □□□, who was overseeing the military operations against Japan in Beijing, agreeing to go hunting in the suburbs with British Ambassador Lampson on the 12th.

The fact that important figures still have leisurely interests in the face of national crisis has "existed since ancient times," according to historical records. The most famous example is the Battle of the Huai River. Not only were the Qin troops far beyond the Great Wall, but they also crossed the Yellow River and directly threatened the Huai River. Yet, Prime Minister Xie An remained composed and played chess without changing his expression. Zhuge Kongming's playing the zither to repel Sima Yi in the novel "Romance of the Three Kingdoms" is also a "leisurely interest" that has been passed down to this day. Up to the present day, when the Shenyang Incident occurred, the young marshal was still in the midst of singing and dancing; during the Battle of Shanghai, there was a sudden decision to develop the Northwest; when Rehe fell, the overseeing figure suddenly moved from the north to the south. These are all examples of the "leisurely interests" of important figures. And the three northeastern provinces, Jinzhou, Yuguan, and Chengde, all changed their colors amidst the leisurely interests of the important figures. What is buying a few ancient books and antiques? Who knows, buying a few ancient books and antiques, or going hunting, might repel enemy troops like Xie An's chess or Zhuge's zither?

Returning Home 238

— Shu Ji

After half a day's journey by water, it was already five o'clock when the small steamboat approached the dock. I stretched languidly in the cabin, leaned on the boatman's shoulder, and jumped onto land; the gentle breeze blowing from the water secretly dispersed the weariness that had accumulated from living in Shanghai for two years. Raising my eyes, I gazed eastward; that city, full of the stench of flesh, the clamor of machinery, the colors of decadence... seemed to be still faintly visible beneath the misty white clouds.

! Ah, farewell, wicked Shanghai!

With a slight sigh, I lifted my feet and strolled along the bank towards the village nestled among the trees nearby. The wheat seedlings by the roadside gently swayed their heads, as if welcoming their long-lost master. The green mountains buried in the afterglow of the setting sun, the stream shimmering with golden light, the fisherman crouched by the river, the shepherd boy riding on the back of an ox, and the scenery that I had previously overlooked, now filled me with wonder. My eyes were like the camera of a greedy photographer, insatiably swiveling in all directions.

With the shyness and joyful demeanor of a newly married bride, I walked into the gate of my home, secretly arousing the astonishment of my neighbors; even at dinner time, they still surrounded my mother, as if trying to ferret out some fresh news.

After nine o'clock, I left my family and went alone into a quiet study. I brewed a pot of tea, invited an elderly man who didn't cough much to chat, while I lay on the bed; a red candle was lit beside the bed. I opened the window, letting the wind blow in, gently shaking the flame; the entire room seemed to tremble. The old man sat beside me, mournfully telling me the stories of the village in the two years since I had left. At first, I was quite excited, but soon, I was disappointed, and tears flowed.

The night deepened, and he lazily left. The room was so quiet that even the sound of mice could be heard. Outside the door, the wild dogs barked madly, each bark striking my heartstrings. The stories that had just been etched on my soul silently unfolded before my eyes: In the late spring season, the rain fell day after day, incessantly.

Mountain torrents erupted丨the dikes broke丨

The water丨buried the fields, submerged the stone steps, the floors, the houses...

Women, children... clinging to wooden rafts, branches, rooftops... crying miserably, their cries broken and intermittent...

················

The water receded.

On the mountains, below the mountains, in the small river, the corpses of water buffaloes were scattered like stars!

Bacteria丨丨Epidemics丨丨Coffins丨丨Welcoming the Gods丨

There was no harvest for the whole year, yet taxes had to be paid.

Land tax! National crisis donations! Militia donations!

The poor! Reactionaries! Executions!

··················

The jumbled, fragmented memories bit at my heart like maggots. The ideal rural life I had been pursuing for two years was destroyed in an instant.

The next morning, before the sun had even climbed to the top of the mountain, I quietly boarded the steamboat again, returning to "wicked Shanghai" as before.

Ramblings from Qu Lu 239

— Zi Zhan

(17) Zhang Taiyan on the Poor and Suffering Classes

Recently, regarding Mr. Zhang Taiyan's attitude towards the revolution, whether he inclined to the right, the left, or any other direction, we do not wish to comment and leave that for future historians. However, it is beyond doubt that Mr. Zhang was one of the most left-leaning and radical figures among the party members when he resided in Tokyo during the Tongmenghui era. This can be said to later generations, and there is evidence in surviving issues of the Min Bao. In his long essay on the morality of revolution, he stated that the morality of today largely changes with one's profession. If we categorize people by their occupations, there are sixteen types: 1) farmers, 2) workers, 3) peddlers, 4) merchants, 5) scholars, 6) artists, 7) intellectuals, 8) soldiers, 9) clerks, 10) advisors, 11) business managers, 12) court officials, 13) regional officials, 14) military officers, 15) government officials, and 16) translators. There are sixteen levels of occupation, and the order of their morality also has sixteen levels. Although it is not uniform, one can get a general idea. From artists upwards, they are generally within the realm of morality. Below intellectuals, few are virtuous. The higher one's position, the further one is from virtue. Living with artists and intellectuals is certainly not as enjoyable as living with scholars; living with scholars is certainly not as enjoyable as living with farmers, workers, peddlers, and merchants; living with employed professionals is certainly not as enjoyable as living with unemployed children. He also said that farmers are the highest in morality. They labor with their minds and bodies, working diligently throughout the year. The income from their fields and gardens is enough to support themselves, and they are unaware of the schemes and deceptions of the world. When they encounter officials, they are very cautious and fearful. If there are greedy and cruel officials who relentlessly extort them, they will rise up in rebellion. And when they die for it, they accept it as if it were candy. Workers are slightly more aware of fraud and deceit. They sometimes cheat the market with shoddy tools and flimsy materials, but they are also very strong and unyielding, no different from farmers. Mr. Zhang directly ranked farmers and workers as the highest in morality, followed by peddlers and small merchants, and then by intellectuals who do not hold high positions. From the so-called famous scholars and intellectuals to the bureaucrats, warlords, and comprador class, the lower they are, the lower they are in morality. As for placing soldiers in the same category as intellectuals, he probably did not know that soldiers come from the farmer and worker classes, and many join the ranks because they are unemployed and have no support. Also, in the Min Bao's anniversary celebration, Mr. Zhang himself wrote a speech discussing the strength of revolutionary spirit, stating that the bandits and secret societies of the poor and suffering classes were the strongest, followed by the intellectuals of the petty-bourgeois class, while bureaucrats and warlords were counter-revolutionary. The text was in vernacular, and a summary is as follows:

The current revolution is commonly called "scholars rebelling," while previous revolutions were commonly called "bandits forming alliances." Bandits have strength, while scholars lack strength; bandits do not rely on officials, while scholars rely on their superiors. Therefore, when bandits rise up, they do not rely on governors and viceroys, while scholars want to rely on governors and viceroys to achieve great things. This is truly foolish. Some people say that scholars are not as good as secret societies, and secret societies are not as good as bandits. In my opinion, let's not talk about the level of knowledge, but bandits never have the intention of relying on officials to rebel, secret societies have a little bit of that intention, and scholars have even more. In terms of their base ambitions and weak self-confidence, they cannot help but feel ashamed compared to secret societies and bandits.

Looking at the history of past revolutions, those who rose up from the grassroots used simple, honest, and diligent people, and swept away the malpractices of the previous dynasty. If powerful vassals invade or powerful ministers usurp power, the politics will be the same as in the previous dynasty, with no reforms at all. Because although the emperor is changed, the officials remain the same. The corrupt and greedy customs of the previous dynasty are passed down and cannot be swept away. The current situation in the officialdom is that microscopic worms and germs are spreading poison everywhere. If it is not a revolution of the common people, how can we avoid these miasmas? If we carefully examine Mr. Zhang's words and look back at the Chinese revolution of the past twenty years, it is not difficult to fairly judge the reasons for the failure of the Xinhai Revolution and to evaluate what achievements the recent revolution has made.

Extended Creative Writing

Crossroads of the Era and Love 240

— Zhang Ziping

"The streetcar was delayed, I'm sorry."

Haiquan replied with a smile. But in his heart, he thought, damn it, does he have to act so bossy?

"You were supposed to be here at twelve o'clock, you should have prepared earlier!..."

Yaoxing's attitude seemed to have softened a bit.

"Hurry up, you still have time."

The young man with the cap said in an old-fashioned tone.

"Yes..."

Seeing Yaoxing's respectful attitude towards this young man, Haiquan quickly took out a bundle of printed materials from under his bed and handed them to Haiquan.

"Hurry to the road behind the Bund Park near the Baidu Bridge, and when you see them shouting slogans, distribute these leaflets to the crowd on that side. There are many dockworkers on that side, it's best to scatter your leaflets to the workers!..."

Haiquan felt a little scared in his heart, but he had to take the large bundle of leaflets. His chest was also thumping.

"Hurry up!"

Tang Yaoxing commanded as if he was issuing orders to him, Haiquan had no choice but to take the streetcar to the Bund with a trembling heart.

Sure enough, near the Baidu Bridge, behind the Bund Park, he saw thirteen or fourteen young people who were supposedly comrades. Some, like him, were holding a bundle of printed materials, some were holding short bamboo poles wrapped in colored paper, the flags for the parade. He saw two female comrades from afar. Their attitude seemed calmer than that of the male comrades. Their attitude of putting life and death out of mind gave Haiquan a lot of inspiration. So he became as nervous as they were. Haiquan glanced at the comrades again, each was pale, like a dying person, and their expression was extremely tense, as if facing a formidable enemy.

Haiquan inadvertently looked across the road, and he found that Li Yixiang and his friends were also pacing back and forth in front of the Japan Mail Steamship Company. They all had their hands behind their backs, holding a book in their hands. When Haiquan saw Mr. Li Yixiang, it was as if he had found a clear spring in the desert, so happy that he wanted to shout. He looked at both ends, and when there were fewer vehicles, he quickly crossed the road and walked to Mr. Yixiang.

"Mr. Li!"

He cried out. He thought that when Li Yixiang saw him, he would be as happy as he was. And he could also show Li Yixiang that he was now participating in practical revolutionary work.

"Oh, oh, oh."

When Li Yixiang saw him, he only said "oh" a few times, and his face showed a kind of displeasure. Haiquan felt directly that Mr. Li was just not saying that he didn't know him. At the same time, he noticed that when Mr. Li looked at the bundle of printed materials in Haiquan's hand, his face showed a look of fear. Li Yixiang frowned, moved his jaw slightly, as if telling him to hurry back to the other side of the road. Seeing Li Yixiang's cold attitude, Haiquan also felt half cold, he inadvertently glanced at the large volume of Western-style books in Mr. Li's hand and recognized it as the Old and New Testaments. The books in the hands of the other two literary figures were Western books, and Haiquan had no mood to examine them further. When he returned to this side of the road, before he had even stood firmly, he saw that the comrades had opened their colored paper flags with slogans written on them, and the leader in front shouted loudly:

"Down with imperialism!"

Silk and Tea Industries Implement Abandoning Tael System and Adopting Yuan System 262

After all commercial businesses in this city obeyed the Ministry of Finance's order to implement the abandonment of the tael system and adoption of the yuan system on the 6th of this month, all transactions are calculated in silver dollars. The purchase and sale of raw silk by Chinese and foreign merchants, the selling price has always used the silver standard. Since foreign banks have stopped dealing in taels, the silk industry also follows the abandonment of the tael system and adoption of the yuan system. All raw silk contracts sold by Chinese silk merchants to foreign firms, the silk prices are calculated in silver taels, are calculated by converting one tael to 7 qian, 1 fen, and 5 li in silver dollars. From today onwards, Chinese and foreign silk merchants negotiate raw silk transactions, all priced in silver dollars.

Artificial Silk Transactions Also Converted to Silver Dollars 263

Foreign firms in this port that sell European and American rayon usually sell rayon based on the listed price and convert it to taels. Therefore, the Rayon Association negotiates transactions in taels. As foreign exchange rates, such as pounds and US dollars, have been converted to silver dollars at a rate of 715 from today, the export quantity is calculated in silver dollars. The quantity exported was 4,929 dan, and the quantity re-exported was 3,864 dan, totaling 8,793 dan. Compared to the 9,599 dan exported and 2,406 dan re-exported in the same quarter last year, totaling 12,005 dan, this represents a decrease of over 3,200 dan. Among the export figures, exports to the United Kingdom and the United States have slightly increased, while exports to Africa have decreased sharply by over 5,500 dan, and France and Hong Kong have also decreased. Re-export figures increased by 1,400 dan compared to the previous quarter. Exports to Russia and the United States increased, while exports to the United Kingdom, France, and Hong Kong all decreased. The export volume of other teas increased by about 4,800 dan in this quarter, and the re-export volume increased by 14,000 dan. The most important factor for the increase in the above figures is that a large amount of brick tea was exported after the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia. The other reason is that last year, tea merchants were in urgent need of funds during the Lunar New Year and had to sell at a loss. Foreign merchants took advantage of the opportunity to purchase in moderation and transport it overseas. As evidenced by the transaction volume in this quarter being less than that in the same quarter last year, and the tea price falling drastically by about 30 taels compared to last year, it can be seen that overseas sales are still not optimistic.

Current Situation of Tunxi Tea Market 264

Tunxi is the center of the tea market in southern Anhui. There are 60-70 tea firms in the town. In recent years, foreign merchants' appetite for goods from Wutun Gaozhuang has been keen, and market prices have also risen. Tea operators are still relatively successful. However, over the years, there have been rapid and drastic changes in the tea routes of various countries, sales appetites have become sincere, and market prices have fallen to their lowest level. Tea firms have suffered, and the impact is no less than that on Wuyuan, but it is also the most severe blow in nearly ten years. Black tea is about to be launched, and green tea is also about to be launched. Tunxi tea firms have a cold attitude, and the wharf is also mainly tightening its release of remittances. At present, there are few firms preparing to open the market. However, upon observing the reason for their coldness, it is found that firms do not increase or decrease their operations due to the tightness of silver. In reality, the overseas tea market has not yet turned around, and market prices have not yet rebounded. The current main points of Tunxi tea firms are two: first, mountain prices must be low, and costs must be reduced; second, the overseas tea market must have a turnaround. If one of the two is feasible, then the number of tea firms opening in Tunxi this year may not be greatly reduced.

Number of Fuliang Tea Firms Reduced Compared to the Past 265

Fuliang black tea suffered significant losses last year due to sluggish overseas sales, sharing the same fate as Qimen black tea. This year, Fuliang tea firms are mostly unable to recover from the heavy losses of the previous year. In addition, the Shanghai wharf is becoming more stringent in its release of remittances to Fuliang, and only a small number of firms have received tea tickets. With limited financial resources, the number of firms has naturally decreased. At present, in addition to the well-established tea firms that do not rely on line payments and can still open their markets as before, the rest are temporarily deciding whether to proceed based on the situation. As of now, there are more than 20 tea firms opening markets in Jiangcun, Pancun, Baimaogang, Yutian, Guixi, Qiongong, and other places in Fuliang. Although there are many others that can open markets, they are all financially weak and hope to obtain low mountain prices and attempt to purchase tea on credit. If silver remains tight and small firms seek cash, then these tea firms may find it difficult to proceed smoothly.

Commentary

Ode to Peace 266

— I

If we are still very concerned about national affairs and still believe in the reports in the newspapers every day, then we can clearly understand that the corner of Northeast China is now full of peace. Obviously, this does not mean that Japanese imperialists have ceased their ambition of aggression, but rather that our China loves peace deeply and is constantly "luring the enemy in deep." However, it is a pity that there is no clear provision as to where the "deep" will reach, and if every "national hero" understands the mystery of this "strategy," then the enemy can be allowed to penetrate all the way to the south bank of the Yellow River.

Thus, this is highlighting China's virtue of deep love of peace.

However, not every Chinese person loves peace. Sometimes, this virtue is a bit unreliable. For example, sometimes if you accidentally step on someone's foot in the tram, it is inevitable to resort to violence. If someone snatches your seat in the theater, it is also inevitable to resort to violence. Even in all other needle-point-sized events, it is common to lose all civility. This is to say that since everyone is Chinese, of course, they will make the most noise, just like the current situation on both sides of the Yangtze River, where people are really killing each other until blood flows like rivers and corpses lie everywhere, which is so lively. From this, it can be seen that Chinese people's love of peace is only for external consumption, while it is not necessary internally.

Under the banner of peace, the three provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang have been offered to Japan as a big stage for wooden puppet shows. The Shanghai war, which sacrificed countless lives, was also "agreed upon" under the banner of peace. The last province, Rehe, will of course be allowed to be invaded by the enemy under the banner of peace. Presumably, closing the iron gate of the Great Wall, in any case, the Volunteers may not completely turn into cannon fodder for a while. If you pack up your valuables and move, you may not be too rushed. However, many poor people are unwilling to "suffer because of peace" and advocate fighting hard, clenching their fists, firmly opposing imperialism, and permanently consolidating peace. However, this kind of cry is ultimately because they have no tongue, and it cannot resound through the clouds for a while. Therefore, everyone can only end up wearing a garland of peace and dancing on the tips of guns and knives.

Peace, many people dream about it day and night. Only most people will one day uncover the illusory curtain of peace.

Shanghai People 267

— Yu

A stack of newspapers has been lying under my desk for several days without being read. It's not that I'm too busy, but I seem to feel that reading the newspaper is a torment. After not reading them for three days, I made it a habit to throw the daily newspapers under my desk. Today, a relative came from afar in the countryside. As a "young" (not old) Shanghainese, I had to invite them to see our splendid world. Opening the current Shen Bao local supplement, I seem to have grown a few years younger. The old tricks that I used to flock to as a student are now being revived in the cry of "Aviation Saves the Nation." According to the instructions of the Public Works Bureau's Film Censorship Committee, children under the age of seventeen are not admitted to cinemas. There are seven or eight dance troupes that use women's flesh as their gimmick. Even more, there is a special note: "Today is the last day. To benefit the audience, there will be an extra performance of American dances. Children under the age of sixteen are not allowed to enter." This indicates that there is a good show to watch here.

Before September 18th, Shanghai was playing these tricks. After the loss of Rehe, Shanghai is still playing these tricks. Except for the January 28th Incident, when the Japanese dared to offend the gods, we ruined our homes to alleviate the disaster and donated silk cotton jackets... to win a patriotic title. Now, Shanghai is still the same Shanghai. We are still playing the old trick of saving the nation without forgetting the sensual.

At the same time, I am fortunate enough to see the headline "The non-resistance general and his family boarded a ship last night and set sail this morning." The culprit who caused the January 28th Shanghai War has quietly gone abroad to play golf. What do Shanghainese think of this? Although I heard that someone dared to throw a bomb at the former large gambling den at No. 181, the general's headquarters before his departure, the general still languidly went to a foreign dance hall to dream butterfly dreams. The general committed a heinous crime but was not harmed in the slightest, and he majestically took his family abroad amid farewells. But to be fair, besides arguing with rickshaw pullers over a single copper coin, Shanghainese have always been generous. Please, General, don't have any lifelong regrets on the Conte Rosso! Don't you see that "Singing and dancing (the singing and dancing of the XXX Dance Troupe) bring peace" has long brought peace to the world. As for taking away a few ancient calligraphy and paintings from the Summer Palace and selling a

Page 20

Naval hospital, that's even less of our concern. Farewell, General, we wish you "smooth sailing and may you turn back to shore!"

Literature and Art

Visiting Nanxiang on Qingming Festival to Commemorate the Traces of War 268

— Zhou Gongmou

Willows greet people, vying to open their eyes. The wind carries the sound of cuckoos, full of resentment. Pennant shadows and paper ashes obscure the wild colors, a desolate smoke shrouds the spring city.

A hundred flowers bloom in anger, covering the slopes. The millet and sorghum are scattered, causing much regret. The remnants of the fortress and broken walls echo with the cries of new ghosts, but the heroic spirit endures, protecting the mountains and rivers.

Wild pears contain tears, willows unfurl green. The wind swirls dust and sand, the grass and trees are rank. The dimmed rivers and mountains evoke thoughts of heroes, regretting the lack of long-term plans to comfort their spirits.

Twenty years of fleeting light evoke a sense of passing waves. Revisit, and the temples are already gray. The desolate Guyi Garden is no longer what it once was, a few weeping willows accompany the dodder.

Died in Vain 269

— Tianxing

According to a telegram from Peiping: "The families and troops of Su, Ma, Li, and Wang, more than a thousand people, have been living in the New World Building since returning from Soviet Russia. Due to the cramped space and extreme filth... more than ten people have died of infectious diseases in recent days..." The subordinates of Su, Ma, Li, and Wang, who resisted for a year and did not die under the hail of bullets, ended up dying of illness in the cramped and filthy New World Building in Peiping. This makes the reporter feel the following thoughts. The troops of Su, Ma, Li, and Wang fiercely resisted the enemy in the snow and ice of the Northeast for a whole year while being ravaged by the brutal Japanese. In the end, although they inevitably suffered a crushing defeat and retreated into Russia due to running out of ammunition and supplies, the fact is clear that they have demonstrated the spirit of the Chinese nation to the world. They have added several pages of glory to China's history, giving the world powers a surprise and giving the brutal Japanese some lessons. How should we, the compatriots who are temporarily living in ease, admire and worship these national heroes who have added glory to the nation? At the very least, I think we should express our respect and sympathy to them! Now, the national heroes Su, Ma, Wang, and Li's troops, who have added glory to the nation, have returned from Moscow; and among them, unfortunately, more than ten people have died of illness due to the cramped and filthy conditions of the New World Building. The national heroes who sacrificed everything for the nation's honor; unfortunately, they suffered a crushing defeat due to running out of ammunition and supplies and returned to their motherland, but even some good treatment was not given to them, and they even died of illness. Regarding this point, I think most of the blame can be attributed to the incompetence of the Chinese government, and a small part can be attributed to the irresponsibility of the Chinese people. In fact, what a big deal is this? Being able to allocate the New World Building to accommodate them returning from Russia is already a great blessing. Isn't the country currently in an economic panic? People are being asked to recognize the emptiness of the national treasury and are rushing to issue national salvation bonds, national salvation funds... and do not have the leisure to entertain the subordinates of Su, Ma, Wang, and Li, who are now irrelevant to them. China now needs people who buy and subscribe to national salvation bonds, not the remaining subordinates of Su, Ma, Li, and Wang who survived the resistance against the brutal Japanese; but, all said and done, it is only unfair to the national heroes who died in the war of resistance against Japan, and the remaining troops and families of Su, Ma, Li, and Wang who survived the sacrifice. The only way to survive is to struggle!

Clerk Communications

Equal Educational Opportunities 270

Mr. Baobao:

After reading your letter, I was reminded of a situation two years ago. I also encountered a similar incident, which I still regret. Therefore, I believe that young people who lost their education early are too unfortunate.

Your letter seems to be a backlash prompted by "unfairness," shouting for many young people who have suffered misfortune but aspire to learn. This is necessary. In such a contradictory society, one can hear the same cries everywhere; but in the end, it is in vain. I believe it can only influence a generation with a small amount of persistence; shouting is shouting, exams are exams, qualifications are still qualifications. No matter how loudly you shout, even if you shout yourself hoarse, those who think they are extraordinary will just "go their own way." They will never be moved to agree with you, or express regret that "you have considerable ability but no diploma."

My old friend K, after graduating from a five-year high school, had to serve society with the knowledge he was not satisfied with due to hardship. He is very capable and performs very well, so he is very competent in his duties. Last year, he wanted to improve his status and once applied for an exam in a certain agency, hoping to obtain a more advantageous position. After all, his fortune was not good, and his luck was bad. He was strictly rejected by the chief examiner: the reason was that "diplomas from unregistered schools are invalid." He - my unfortunate old friend - stated that all schools were unregistered four years ago, and he graduated four years ago. His statement clearly hoped that there would be room for flexibility, but the chief examiner, who claimed to be "selecting true talent," only shook his head repeatedly, and finally there was an inevitable fierce debate. He ran away in disappointment and told me about his experience. Finally, he added: "I really don't understand why they take exams so seriously? After admission, it's 'official business is handled, no official business means reading newspapers and dozing off.' Why are they so lax? Those jobs are not something ordinary people can't do, why bother so much about the exam?" I smiled silently, smiling at him - my Mr. K - he already understands that society is like this, but he needs my explanation.

"This is a contradictory phenomenon of society. In this contradictory society, you have to be smarter, say contradictory things, and do contradictory things to be a 'modern' person" - this is how I explained it to him.

Sir, what do you think? It is indeed very difficult for people like us who do not have the strength or sufficient time to pursue higher learning. If you think that a square hat qualification - within your possible range - is at least necessary, or that it is absolutely necessary to have super deep, try your best to move forward. But I want to ask you to use a microscope to examine the entire situation of society carefully, you will definitely see the owners of square hats complaining that there are too few pawnshops and worrying about where to pawn their square hats!

It's not that I like to say unmotivated and unproductive words. For people like us who have no power, too much knowledge is useless in business. Just a considerable degree is enough. (Perhaps you think otherwise, because I don't understand your situation, please forgive me.) I often think... In the current situation, which is more important: knowledge or ability (ability refers to economics and experience)? My prejudice is that knowledge is indeed necessary, but ability is even more indispensable. Having knowledge without ability is like having a boat without oars, which won't work. So I dare not say that what the students of the two top business schools you mentioned will be completely suitable for our country's society in the future! I am even more confident that it is not that there is no true talent and therefore incompetent, and that those who have ability but lack knowledge cannot stand and make a living. Then, why should we waste time and lose our jobs to engage in this metaphysics? Therefore, you do not have to worry about the business school. You must know that the true meaning of the two words "knowledge" is that you can learn and ask at any time and anywhere. Only ability is achieved through struggle.

Struggle! Friend! Struggle hard! I wish you

Happiness Jiang Rendi

Editor's Note: Mr. Jiang said that the letter from Mr. Baobao, published in this column on April 4th, is a backlash of "unfairness." But isn't this letter from Mr. Jiang also the same? Moreover, the degree of indignation is excessive. In this kind of society, naturally, everyone can't avoid complaining! You said, "Having knowledge without ability is like having a boat without oars;" that's certainly true. But we think that "Having knowledge without ability is like a big boat, but it also has sails and oars," of course, it is difficult to move an inch. But "Having ability without knowledge is like a small boat, even if it has two oars," it will inevitably capsize in the face of wind and waves. Only "Having both knowledge and ability is like a big boat, equipped with sails and oars," can it ride the wind and waves. Therefore, we still cannot help but shout the slogan of "Equal Educational Opportunities," hoping that people in society will shout like this, and shout loudly. The result of this shout may not be equal to zero!

Time in a Dream (Part 27) 271

— Qin Shouou

When he was treading through the snow, he was still painfully worrying and repenting, no wonder he couldn't get excited. How would Jufen know? Estimating that he was always troubled by other things, she deliberately put on various expressions of excitement and joy to please him, but this only increased his pain. He almost wanted to leave her and escape from the park alone.

"...Suddenly my stomach hurts a lot, let's go back quickly!" Although he didn't escape alone first, he couldn't stay in the park any longer, so he made up a lie and tricked Jufen out of the park, sadly saying goodbye.

On the day when the snow in Zhaofeng Park completely melted into flowing water, Wu Yi had taken his wife and son from Shanghai to Nanjing, and his position as Dean of Academic Affairs at XX University was also resigned without a trace. At that time, it happened to be the beginning of the spring semester, and Wu Yi accepted the appointment of the XX Political School a week after arriving in Nanjing.

The problem of occupation was solved without any effort, but how to solve his piece of lost passion? He first went to the Confucius Temple every day to listen to the singing of those little girls who "know nothing of the Han Dynasty, let alone the Wei and Jin Dynasties," hoping to find a new pleasure, but he got tired of it in less than five days. Then he tried to use playing cards with friends as a way to relieve his sorrow, but he didn't succeed either.

One day, he passed through a narrow and secluded alley and saw a burly man, dressed in rags, bareheaded and barefoot like a coolie, drinking until his face was as red as pasted red paper, laughing and singing all the way as he crashed out of a small hotel.

"Hey! Dad of Ada! There's no rice for dinner, hurry up and find a way!" A woman with a sallow complexion came and grabbed the big man's arm, begging him with a smile.

"Haha! Let's talk about it at night!... Innkeeper, bring it over, yellow..." The big man didn't seem to hear it, forcefully opening the woman's hand and staggering away.

"Haha! Drinking is really the most delicious!" Wu Yi muttered to himself very proudly, hiding aside. Immediately, he suddenly realized that in the vast world, the only thing that can really relieve people's worries is "only wine." From then on, he made drinking a daily routine, and often drank himself so drunk that he was unconscious. Nanjing Su Xin Jian
