Film Special

New Works from the Anglo-German Film Industry Union 272

— Xinpu

"Peach Blossom Village" and "Spring River in the Flower Moon Night" Arrive in Shanghai

For the past twenty-five years, the global film industry has been dominated by the United States. However, in recent years, Germany, which is unwilling to lag behind, has been struggling and striving to compete with the United States. Although they have strong ambition, they are afraid that they do not have enough talent, so they have united with the United Kingdom to use the strength of the two countries to compete for the dominance of the world film industry. The companies that have cooperated are currently holding the reins of the film industry in both countries, one is Ufa of Germany, and the other is Gaumont of the United Kingdom.

"Peach Blossom Village" (Happy Ever After) and "Spring River in the Flower Moon Night" (Tell Me To-night) are the new works from the Anglo-German film industry union's first attempt to show their edge. When they were publicly screened in Europe and the United States, not only did the European media vigorously promote and praise them, but the American newspapers and magazines were also full of a surprising tone. These two films have now been transported to China. Let me first give readers a brief report on the contents of the two films.

The story of "Peach Blossom Village" is a story of a love triangle in the proletariat, with some bitterness in the sweetness. "Spring River in the Flower Moon Night" describes the romance of a singer. In terms of consciousness, these two films do not have anything special, but they can use beautiful photography, novel music, clever editing, and profound description to make two purely artistic masterpieces. What is most commendable is that they can make the most of the natural beauty of the countryside in these two films, giving rise to endless pleasure.

A London newspaper said: "Peach Blossom Village" has a screening time of eighty-six minutes, and "Spring River in the Flower Moon Night" has a screening time of ninety-one minutes; but when it was released, many friends said why the film was so short, as if it had been screened in two or thirty minutes!" The meaning is that the film is so good that the viewers spent the actual time without realizing it. From this point of view, we can prove the enthusiasm of Western Europeans in welcoming these two films.

Regarding the actors, I may as well report first. The main characters of "Peach Blossom Village" are Lil Dagover (the heroine of "Dragon Soaring Phoenix Dance", who has now gone to Hollywood) and Jacques Holbert (the main character in "Happy Marriage").

The main character of "Spring River in the Flower Moon Night" is Jan Kiepura, a singing titan worshipped by European men, women, and children. Among the several actors mentioned above, only Lil Dagover and Jacques Holbert are known to us, and the others have not yet met the people of Shanghai, but Jan Kiepura's singing voice and all the other actors will leave a deep impression in the minds of thousands of movie fans, just like these two films.

Film Review

Review of "The Sign of the Cross" 273

— Linghe

The Sign of the Cross

A tragedy promoting Christianity

Excellent directing, excellent performance

After watching "The Ten Commandments" or "The King of Kings", we know that Cecil B. DeMille is a skilled bourgeois film artist and also a most loyal Christian. Of course, any religion has its believers, and many of these believers try their best to preach for the religion they believe in. Moreover, if we believe that a certain religion is often used by authorities to become a tool of rule, then this "preaching" has its political significance.

Cecil B. DeMille, like Griffith, the director of "Seventh Heaven", has had great success in their film art field, and at the same time, they have tried to explain the conflicts or contradictions of the current society under the "glory" of "God", at least to make the audience forget reality with this "spiritual influence". Therefore, we can definitely say that they are only technically successful, and their ideology can only win the praise of the smallest part of the people.

Undoubtedly, we can find the most obvious evidence in this "Tne Sign of the Cross". The Roman dynasty at the peak of feudal power may have been as promiscuous and brutal as described in this drama. They sang and rejoiced in the burning city, they were extremely promiscuous, they fed the people to the beasts and regarded it as a carnival, they cheered and laughed at the cruelty of the people's melee. But these people were a flock of sheep, they only succumbed under extreme tyranny, and did not dare to resist in the slightest. A group of so-called "loving" and "kind" Christians had to die sadly in the loud sound of hymns. Obviously, this only illustrates the horror of feudal power, and does not give any slight criticism to feudal power directly. On the contrary, it even praises the great merits of feudal power. Especially in order to insert a love story, a high-ranking official of a dynasty was actually bewitched by female beauty and gladly sacrificed himself with the Christian dissidents. It is really a so-called whimsical idea, not knowing its meaning. Perhaps it is praising the "sacred" and "great" love.

But the director's skill is really extraordinarily successful. After watching it, all the "sensual" and "beasts" necessary for current American films are fully used, but they are not forced insertions, but are important parts of the drama, becoming the natural development of the plot. That kind of directing technique, although (it is his old way, but still does not lose its perfect effect. If we want to illustrate with examples, then the palace in the flames at the beginning, the beautiful shot when the captain of the guard entered the play. After a young Christian was arrested, Mark's knocking on the door of the woman's house was intentionally tense. The queen and Mark stood in front of the grape basin to talk about love. The cries in the fire trap. The sadness of the large number of Christians before execution, and the solemn singing, and the light that poured down from above. Others, such as the child's laughter in the solemn sermon, and the ignorant laughter at the time of execution, and the relative writing with the old man, and the heroine's weeping, are all the best scenes that can move people to tears. Furthermore, the director does not forget the cross everywhere in the play, which is of course the center of the play, but it is also very vivid. The skillful and appropriate performance is of course due to the director's command, but the achievements of several important roles must be admitted anyway. Other aspects are all excellent, and there is no need to say more.

In short, this is a film that is most successful in performance techniques. In this film, the characteristics of bourgeois films can be seen. Although we cannot ignore the history of American films and the perfection of all its production conditions. However, in the intention of the play, they are all estranged from us, at least for the general non-Christians, they may not be able to be greatly "influenced".

Finally, I think this film title should not be translated as "Luogong Spring Colors", because it does not match the content of the film too much, and it loses the focus of the play. Moreover, good films are definitely not called upon by the name of "fragrant and beautiful".

Famous Soviet Female Director 274

— Shiyi

15th Anniversary of Drama Life

This year is the 15th anniversary of the drama life of Natalya Sats, a famous female director in Moscow. The Soviet Ministry of Education and the Theater Department plan to jointly hold a celebration. In 1918, the lady was only fourteen years old and organized the First Moscow Soviet Children's Theater. In 1921, the Moscow Children's Theater was established, and the lady served as director, playwright, and set designer. Since the establishment of the theater to this day, a total of 3 million children have watched the theater, and 42 new dramas have been compiled, among which the two dramas "Black Child and Monkey" have been performed as many as 250 times. (Tas news agency, 11th)

Review of "The Horror Hole" Doctorx 275

— Heart

"The Horror Hole," originally named Doctor X, was one of the biggest films of the leading national company last year. Carlton has been running previews for over a month; it finally premiered yesterday. Before the film began, there were ten stage performances of song and dance.

Regarding the song and dance, I am not in a position to comment much here. However, I believe that the selection of performers for this "World Song and Dance Troupe," although including some actors from the previous "All-American Song and Dance Troupe," is more brilliant than the previous two. Another point to note is that this time it doesn't overemphasize the women's legs.

The plot of "The Horror Hole" leaves us with a very vague impression. It says that murders often occur when the moon is full. A Doctor X and a newspaper reporter are trying to find out the truth. So, in Doctor X's laboratory, he gathers four scientists, believing that the murderer is one of them. Therefore, he has a male and female servant stage a fake murder, intending to use scientific methods to detect the murderer's mood and evidence. His deputy is a disabled man. The first night fails, and one of the scientists is killed instead. On the second night, because the female servant is ill, he asks his daughter to play the role of the victim in the fake murder. It is then discovered that the murderer is the disabled deputy. The case is handled entirely by the reporter, and Doctor X's daughter marries the reporter.

The purpose of this script is to instill terror and demonstrate the omnipotence of science. There are inherent irrationalities that are beyond human understanding; for example, the motive for Doctor X's research and the reasons for the murderer's killings are not clearly explained. The terrifying parts in the entire film are actually few and far between, and it deviates from the scope of detective films. However, the various difficulties fully demonstrate the director's competence, with surprising suspense set up everywhere. However, sometimes the revelations come too quickly. Although his intention is to make people feel humorous, using laughter to regulate the tense atmosphere, it actually has the disadvantage of being too scattered and lax. There are also quite a few minor flaws. In ordinary films, these would not be regrettable, but in a horror film, they appear as too large of loopholes. Therefore, the director can be considered successful overall, but a failure in parts, especially since he should not have used a humorous approach, undermining much of the serious terror.

The actors are generally above average. In horror films, inner expressions are hardly possible. Only Fay Wray, who plays Doctor X's daughter, is somewhat better. Lee Tracy, who plays the newspaper reporter, frankly fails to live up to his past reputation, which is annoying.

The sets are ordinary. The displays and equipment in those scientific laboratories are very good and can rival those in "Frankenstein." The lighting is also good, and the work on the camera is commendable. The scene transitions are good, but errors can also be found, such as conflicts in time. There seems to be too much dialogue. The pronunciation is too heavy, also losing the possibility of terror.

### The People Regard Food as Heaven 276

— Yu Lun

Gary Cooper threw a grand banquet one day, inviting sixty couples. He prepared a good band and carpets for them to dance. But that day, the banquet adopted a freestyle approach, that is, putting various foods on the table, allowing guests to take whatever they wanted. The dance music played and played, but no couple came out to dance. They just surrounded the table and feasted!

### Fake Turks, Real Bath 277

— Yu Lun

One day, Pickford went to the countryside to shoot location scenes. Fairbanks, dressed as a Turk, lay in wait on the road, wanting to scare her. Her ox cart indeed arrived beside him, so he jumped out and shouted at her: "Hands up! Put everything down, and I'll spare you." Before he finished speaking, a torrential rain suddenly arrived. Thus, this fake Turk got an outdoor Turkish bath first!

### Film Novel Tara Kanova (2) 278

— Plum Blossom

During the hail of gunfire, amidst the shouts of people and neighing of horses, Orlov also recalled Catherine's tenderness towards him. He commanded the Imperial Russian army, launching a major offensive against Turkey. After days and nights of madness and slaughter, Imperial Russia finally achieved final victory.

On this day, Orlov was in the camp, drinking and making merry with his soldiers. Everyone was beating war drums and singing songs of victory. Suddenly, a disheveled, ragged Gypsy girl wandered into the camp. She had bewitching giant eyes, a lovely figure, and crimson lips. In particular, her demeanor of unsettled panic was, in Orlov's eyes, even more unusually charming. Especially in the military camp, it was as if encountering a spring in the desert. From that moment on, a deep, lovely shadow was embedded in Orlov's heart. This Gypsy girl, she was fleeing the violence of those fully armored warriors, and then she rashly ran into Orlov's camp; at first, she was a little frightened, but when Orlov stared at her intently, she suddenly felt a sense of shame. After a while, she recovered her usual lively state and began to sing her charming song. Her dancing posture while singing, and her soft and moving tone, penetrated deeply into the depths of Orlov's heart, word by word! He was lost; he didn't know what to do with his heart.

It was dusk, and the sounds of the battlefield brought some desolate air. Orlov was contemplating how to deal with this enchanting girl, and in a blink of an eye, she had disappeared. He felt an indescribable emptiness.

About a week later, Count Shuffalov, who had lost favor at the court, was sent to the front line. He was walking around the camp on patrol when he accidentally encountered this alluring Gypsy girl. Her two eyes, with their enchanting magic, were just like those of Princess Posietty, who was living in seclusion in the monastery. Shuffalov observed carefully and felt that she not only had Princess Posietty's appearance but also Princess Posietty's spirit. He thought to himself, "Since Princess Posietty refuses to come out against Catherine, I can use this Gypsy girl as a tool to oppose Catherine." (To be continued)
